From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Mar  1 14:41:27 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 1 Mar 2005 14:41:27 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] server-status, server-info : where were you all my life?
Message-ID: <20050301224127.GA3915@gate.kl-ic.com>


A Neat Trick with Apache:  This is  helpful if you are administering
or learning about your apache server.

In your apache server control file, /etc/httpd/conf/httpd.conf for
redhat, you will find two containers (?) that can be uncommented:
<Location /server-status> and <Location /server-info> .  You then
set the "Allow from: lines, for example:

<Location /server-status>
    SetHandler server-status
    Order deny,allow
    Deny from all
    #Allow from .example.com
    Allow from 127.0.0.1 .kl-ic.com
</Location>

Server-info is similar.  This allows me to observe the /server-status
from my server, vcolo, and from any of the machines inside my home
network kl-ic.com , like so:

httpd://vcolo/server-status/
httpd://vcolo/server-info/

The first gives me real time information on who is doing what to my
server right now, while the latter tells me how apache is configured
in enormous detail.  Wow!

You may want to set the flag  "ExtendedStatus On".

-----
Note, my system was missing a library:

 /lib/libcom_err.so.3

I copied over /usr/kerberos/lib/libcom_err.so.3.0 from another machine,
and symbolically linked it.  

----
Webalizer is also handy, for longer term statistics.  See Carla's
"Linux Cookbook" for how to install that.

----

Keith

and perl scripts.  One thing I watching is the maillog with colorize (
perl script ).  Where this goes bad is when logrotate moves the file out
from under colorize , ie. closes the file then opens a new one with the
same name.
   I thought there was a signal that could be sent ( via. kill/killall )  
that caused a process to restart.  But when I tried HUP/SIGHUP it killed
the whole process.  Something in the back brain said HUP ( hangup ) was
the ticket.  Looking in the man pages ( man 7 signal ) I find nothing I
recognize as the proper signal.
   So is there a method that will cause a process to restart?

A "stopped" process (suspended w/ ^Z or "kill -STOP") can
be restarted with "kill -CONT". But if ps(1) shows the
process state as "D", you're pretty much hosed.

>>>>> "Roderick" == Roderick A Anderson <raanders at acm.org> writes:

Roderick> We monitor several mail spool systems using a ssh connection
Roderick> (from a Windows box that runs What's up Gold using PuTTY )

Roderick> one with the same name.  I thought there was a signal that
Roderick> could be sent ( via. kill/killall ) that caused a process to
Roderick> restart.  But when I tried HUP/SIGHUP it killed the whole
Roderick> process.  Something in the back brain said HUP ( hangup )
Roderick> was the ticket.  Looking in the man pages ( man 7 signal ) I
Roderick> find nothing I recognize as the proper signal.  So is there
Roderick> a method that will cause a process to restart?

Signals need the appropriate signal handler in the application
receiving them.  In your case, you want the application to close and
reopen a particular filename.  If the application doesn't provide this
signal handling, you might need to resort to the start/stop init
scripts (in Debian, they are found in /etc/init.d/).  The usual
interface with those is:

  # /etc/init.d/foo restart

where "foo" is the name of the service-start/stopping script.

Maybe that'll work for you.

From srau at rauhaus.org  Wed Mar  2 09:30:04 2005
From: srau at rauhaus.org (Stafford A. Rau)
Date: Wed, 2 Mar 2005 09:30:04 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Restart a 'hung'(?) process
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0503011627360.5754-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0503011627360.5754-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
Message-ID: <20050302173004.GE21264@rauhaus.org>

* Roderick A. Anderson <raanders at acm.org> [050301 16:38]:
> Where this goes bad is when logrotate moves the file out
> from under colorize , ie. closes the file then opens a new one with the
> same name.

You might want to check out swatch (http://www.sourceforge.net/swatch):

====
NOTES

Upon receiving a ALRM or HUP signal swatch will re-read the
configuration file and restart, except when used with the --daemon
command line option where it will simply exit.  Swatch will terminate
gracefully when it receives a QUIT, TERM, or INT signal.
====

You could then fire off script in the "postrotate" option in your
logrotate configuration that will send swatch a HUP sig.

--Stafford

Device shows up as:  /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1

When I run `umount /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1` I get the

umount: /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1: device is busy

umount: /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1: device is busy
umount: /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1: device is busy

Here is my /etc/mtab:

/dev/sda1 /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1 subfs
rw,noexec,nosuid,nodev,sync,fs=floppyfss,procuid 0 0
/dev/sdb1 /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1 subfs
rw,noexec,nosuid,nodev,sync,fs=floppyfss,procuid 0 0
/dev/sda1 /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1 subfs
rw,noexec,nosuid,nodev,sync,fs=floppyfss,procuid 0 0

Any help is greatly appreciatted!

From russj at dimstar.net  Wed Mar  2 10:06:47 2005
From: russj at dimstar.net (Russ Johnson)
Date: Wed, 02 Mar 2005 10:06:47 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Cannot umount USB
In-Reply-To: <s225883f.035@ohsu.edu>
References: <s225883f.035@ohsu.edu>
Message-ID: <422600B7.5000605@dimstar.net>

Jon Bridenbaugh wrote:

>umount: /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1: device is busy
>umount: /media/usb-storage-0000185073:0:0:0p1: device is busy
>

This message is usually caused by something holding open a file on that 
device. It could be as simple as a terminal open with a current working 
directory that in on the device.

Keep in mind that open files are copied to memory, so the fact that the 
device isn't there doesn't matter.

In fact, you should never remove a device prior to unmounting it. When 
you do that, you don't allow the system to close the filesystem, and 
could cause corruption. When you reinsert the device, the file system 
could be marked dirty and would need to be cleaned with fsck before 
being mounted.

Thinking about it a little more, it could be the fact that the device 
was removed while mounted that caused this problem in the first place.

Russ

From cstevens at gencom.us  Wed Mar  2 10:41:23 2005
From: cstevens at gencom.us (D. Cooper Stevenson)
Date: Wed, 02 Mar 2005 10:41:23 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] disk under software mirror died
In-Reply-To: <1109787248.2213.11.camel@rhws.theplatinumrule.com>
References: <1109787248.2213.11.camel@rhws.theplatinumrule.com>
Message-ID: <1109788883.10626.45.camel@localhost>

This kind of issue isn't hard to resolve but it may take a few steps to
get your system booting. I am working under the assumption that /dev/hdb
is an exact copy of /dev/hda. If it were me I would simply remove hda;
it's dead so get it out of there. Then:

  * Cable /dev/hdb to be the new /dev/hda

  * Update the BIOS if not automaticly done

  * Try to boot

The system will likely not boot at this point as the master boot record
is not updated but it never hurts to try and can save time. If the
system doesn't boot then:

  * Boot to Knoppix CD

  * Run GRUB (probably) or LILO to configure Master Boot Record Here's a
nice bootloader guide:


http://www.gentoo.org/doc/en/handbook/handbook-x86.xml?part=1&chap=10

Let me know how it turns out.


-Coop

From plug at merlot.com  Wed Mar  2 10:18:11 2005
From: plug at merlot.com (Kurt Sussman)

Subject: [PLUG] OT: Cellphone provider recomendations?
In-Reply-To: <42237A8F.3010701@servuhome.net>
References: <42237A8F.3010701@servuhome.net>
Message-ID: <20050302181811.GZ12920@merlot.com>

Brent Jones (brent at servuhome.net) typed this ...
> Off-topic, but I'm fed up with my current provider (ATT/Cingular)
> ...
> I've heard T-mobile is decent, as well as Nextel.
> But I was wondering what PLUGgers have experience with.

Sorry for the delayed response, I was roaming. #:)

I've had GTE (which became Verizon), Cingular, ATT (before and during
the merger) and T-Mobile, scattered across three states.

My GTE/Verizon experience is from the dark ages of cellular, pre-1990,
obviously not relevant. Cingular and ATT both gave me the usual "there's
a tower right there!" BS when I complained (all the time) about no
coverage. I started with T-Mobile in Hawaii and it was great (that's the
only place where they owned their own network; I think they sold it
though).

So when I cancelled ATT (they cancelled my contract for free because I
complained regularly and articulately), I bought a Sidekick II on
T-Mobile (from Amazon: free after rebates). My plan is $40/month plus
$20 for unlimited data. There's an ssh clinet for it but it's rarely
useful from the places I go. Voice is good, coverage is good (they roam
on Cingular when you leave town), and customer service has been good so
far (it was great in Hawaii, but that's because you always go to a local
call center and customer service is almost always great in Hawaii).

So I'm happy with T-Mobile, but when Nextel has some more featureful
phones, I'd like to give them a try. Their coverage is great as long as
you're near large-scale construction... they like to make sure their
core market is covered. OTOH Sprint will probably try to cut Nextel's
costs to make them more profitable, and that will impact voice quality
for sure.

HTH.

--Kurt

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Mar  2 11:27:16 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Wed, 2 Mar 2005 11:27:16 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] dnotify detects directory changes
Message-ID: <20050302192716.GA21489@gate.kl-ic.com>


"dnotify" is a program that detects changes to directories (like file
changes or deletes) and executes a script.   I've had problems with
ppp deleting /etc/ppp/pam-secrets (even with pam-secrets set to 400
and /etc/ppp set to 500).  So I set up a call in /etc/inittab :

  papd:2345:respawn:/etc/ppp/papkeeper
  
The papkeeper script contains (among other things):

 /usr/bin/dnotify -D /etc/ppp -e /etc/ppp/papcopy

And the papcopy script contains:

 fpap=/etc/ppp/pap-secrets
 fpapb=/etc/ppp/pap-secrets.bak
 logr="/usr/bin/logger -i -p syslog.err"

 if [ ! -f $fpap ]; then
   $logr -t papkeeper "$fpap replaced"
   /bin/cp $fpapb $fpap
 fi

The inittab respawn line makes sure that there is always one running
copy of my papkeeper script, restarting it if it dies.  The dnotify
program calls the script /etc/ppp/papcopy every time there is a change
to the /etc/ppp directory, or any file in it.  If dnotify terminates,
so does the script, and init respawns it.  dnotify uses existing
structures in the kernel to sleep until something changes;  it does
not need to poll, does not modify the kernel or add modules, and as
it is sleeping most of the time it is not a CPU hog.  It typically
reacts in fractions of a second to file disappearances.

The papcopy script is called for any change in the /etc/ppp
directory, but it ignores all changes except the disappearance
of /etc/ppp/pap-secrets .   That causes it to throw a message to
/var/log/messages , and copy the file from a backup.

Someday, I will find out what I've misconfigured in pppd.  The exact
timing of the dnotify messages to /var/log/messages, in relation to
the messages from pppd itself, will be a big help in that.  But for
now, dnotify is a useful tool for reacting to various file changes; 
when I get time, I will set it to monitoring my wiki and capturing
possible wikispam events.

You can learn more about dnotify at:

http://www.student.lu.se/~nbi98oli/dnotify.html

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs


From mikeraz at patch.com  Wed Mar  2 11:37:42 2005
From: mikeraz at patch.com (Michael Rasmussen)
Date: Wed, 2 Mar 2005 11:37:42 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Restart a 'hung'(?) process
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0503021048250.9955-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0503011627360.5754-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
	<Pine.LNX.4.33.0503021048250.9955-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
Message-ID: <20050302193742.GG2184@patch.com>

Roderick A. Anderson wrote:
> The longer term plan , which may or may not work , is to have the colorize
> script run as a daemon and output to a socket or port that a monitoring 
> program or terminal can connect to and display the output.  I think this 
> is similar to a RSS feed but without the XML.

What about having your log information sent to a pipe and having the log watch
program monitor that?

For example in /etc/syslog.conf modify like:
  authpriv.*      /var/log/secure
  authpriv.*      |/var/log/logpipe

then have colorize monitor logpipe

create logpipe with `mkfifo /var/log/logpipe`

You don't fill up space with the pipe so you don't need to log rotate it.  The log
rotation won't affect your monitoring process. No need to hup or whatever.

Did you initially say that colorize was a Perl thing?  You could edit the code to
install whatever signal handler you'd like...

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Mar  2 13:11:03 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Wed, 2 Mar 2005 13:11:03 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Dead hard drives and the Ultimate Boot CD
Message-ID: <20050302211103.GA22335@gate.kl-ic.com>


I just had a 250G Maxtor fail on me - sort of.  Took it all the
way down to repartitioning and re-mkfs'ing, and it kept throwing
read access errors.  

I found a handy tool.

The Ultimate Boot CD (http://ubcd.sourceforge.net/) has dozens of
DOS-oid manufacturer's diagnostics disk images on it, including the
Maxtor "PowerMax" tool.  I booted from the CD, and PowerMax told me
my drive had an unrecoverable error.  While I could have shipped the
drive back for replacement, I decided to clean off my sensitive data
with a low level format (also part of the PowerMax suite) before I
let Maxtor see it.  This took 26 hours;  however, when I was done the
error was gone.  I ran the Maxtor diags for a day, then partitioned
and formatted the drive (reiserfs) and I am now running Linux 
read/write tests.  I will do about 40 full-drive tests, lasting
about a week, before I try re-using this disk again.  If it errors
out again, and I have to return it, at least my data will be
multiply overwritten.

So, if you have a dead Maxtor disk, give UBCD and PowerMax a try.
You may not get your data back (that is why you do backups), but you
may get a functional drive.

Keith

Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993

Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From larry.brigman at gmail.com  Wed Mar  2 13:35:10 2005
From: larry.brigman at gmail.com (Larry Brigman)
Date: Wed, 2 Mar 2005 13:35:10 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Dead hard drives and the Ultimate Boot CD
In-Reply-To: <20050302211103.GA22335@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20050302211103.GA22335@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <ca51655305030213356c0a6d21@mail.gmail.com>

On Wed, 2 Mar 2005 13:11:03 -0800, Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> wrote:
> 
> I just had a 250G Maxtor fail on me - sort of.  Took it all the
> way down to repartitioning and re-mkfs'ing, and it kept throwing
> read access errors.
> 
> I found a handy tool.
> 
> The Ultimate Boot CD (http://ubcd.sourceforge.net/) has dozens of
> DOS-oid manufacturer's diagnostics disk images on it, including the
> Maxtor "PowerMax" tool.  I booted from the CD, and PowerMax told me
> my drive had an unrecoverable error.  While I could have shipped the
> drive back for replacement, I decided to clean off my sensitive data
> with a low level format (also part of the PowerMax suite) before I
> let Maxtor see it.  This took 26 hours;  however, when I was done the
> error was gone.  I ran the Maxtor diags for a day, then partitioned
> and formatted the drive (reiserfs) and I am now running Linux
> read/write tests.  I will do about 40 full-drive tests, lasting
> about a week, before I try re-using this disk again.  If it errors
> out again, and I have to return it, at least my data will be
> multiply overwritten.
> 
> So, if you have a dead Maxtor disk, give UBCD and PowerMax a try.
> You may not get your data back (that is why you do backups), but you
> may get a functional drive.
> 
This type of error condition is all too common.  It is caused by an interrupted
write (writing while power is not stable).  Depending on how the power changed
during the writing it may affect one or more sectors/tracks.  Excessive reading
of these bad (read mis-written) sectors can cause the drive to report a smart
trip.

There are only two ways to fix this type of problem.  
1) write over the area again ignoring errors. Sorry you data is already gone.
2) Manufacture utility to low level format the disk.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Mar  2 17:30:09 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Wed, 2 Mar 2005 17:30:09 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] dnotify detects directory changes
Message-ID: <20050303013009.GA23899@gate.kl-ic.com>


Keith Lofstrom wrote:
> "dnotify" is a program that detects changes to directories (like file
> changes or deletes) and executes a script.\

Dan Young wrote:
> Some distributions (Fedora and Ubuntu, that I know of) are incorporating
> Gamin, related to FAM, which monitors files and directories:
> http://www.gnome.org/~veillard/gamin/index.html
>
> Also, Novell's Robert Love has been working on inotify, a replacement
> for dnotify:
> http://www.kernel.org/pub/linux/kernel/people/rml/inotify/README
>
> The differences between all of these are lost on me, I'm just providing
> relevant linkage.

Keith responds:

Gamin is an alternative to FAM, which is an API for user space
C programs.  The "dnotify" I was talking about is a user application
that can be called from a shell.

Robert Love's "inotify" is a replacement for the "dnotify" kernel
code, and is also not a user application.  Yes, "dnotify" is two
different things, a set of kernel code to track files, and an
executable that (for now) uses the kernel code.  The "dnotify"
user program probably can be adapted to the newer (and still
experimental) inotify code when that becomes generally available.

Robert Love's rather childish rant about the evils of the "dnotify"
kernel code is offputting;  however, he does point out that a file
system with a directory being watched with the "dnotify" program
and using the "dnotify" kernel code may be difficult to unmount. 
My scripts are looking at stuff in /etc, which is always mounted
when init is running;  however, in general users probably should
make sure all dnotify processes pointing at a filesystem are stopped
before trying to unmount that filesystem.

The inotify kernel code seems to penetrate pretty deep into the
linux virtualization layer.  So,  I wonder how compatible it is
with various high-performance file systems, and whether that (or
Mr. Love's fetching ways ) will slow it's general acceptance?  

Keith

Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993

Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From cstevens at gencom.us  Wed Mar  2 21:26:06 2005
From: cstevens at gencom.us (D. Cooper Stevenson)
Date: Wed, 02 Mar 2005 21:26:06 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] disk under software mirror died
In-Reply-To: <1109806030.1208.3.camel@rhws.theplatinumrule.com>
References: <1109787248.2213.11.camel@rhws.theplatinumrule.com>
	<1109788883.10626.45.camel@localhost>
	<1109806030.1208.3.camel@rhws.theplatinumrule.com>
Message-ID: <1109827566.11711.51.camel@localhost>

On Wed, 2005-03-02 at 15:27 -0800, Mike De La Mater wrote:


> 
> I've carefully been through the directions and set grub to boot from the
> proper image on the correct drive, but it still will not boot. fdisk
> shows the partitions as part of the RAID array, still.


Okay. This and below makes things somewhat tighter but within tolerance.

I have a (short) checklist of things to look for:

  1) Is the primary partition marked "bootable?" This usually does not
matter these days but never hurts to have it there. Use fdisk.

> 
> I'm using knoppix to copy off the home directory to get ready to install
> new drives. 


  2) Are all the partitions there with data intact? I ask as this was a
part of a RAID set. This adds a layer of variability that should be
checked.

 
Finally, a question: do you get to the GRUB graphical menu upon starting
our computer? If so, GRUB is configured correctly. If not, try your grub
configuration again. Remember, you want to boot to your /boot

Here's an example of my /boot/grub/grub.conf:

  # For booting Primary Desktop Computer
  title Personal Desktop Computer
   root (hd0,4)
  kernel (hd0,4)/kernel-2.6.10 root=/dev/ram0 init=/linuxrc
real_root=/dev/hda1 splash=verbose hdc=scsi-cd vga=0x317 splash=verbose
video=vfb
  initrd (hd0,4)/initrd-2.6.10

   # For booting Mosix Cluster Node
   title Mosix Cluster Kernel
   root (hd0,4)
   kernel (hd0,4)/kernel-2.4.26-om1 root=/dev/ram0 init=/linuxrc
real_root=/dev/hda1 splash=verbose hdc=ide-cd vga=0x317
   initrd (hd0,4)/initrd-2.4.26-om1

Note that my /etc/fstab looks like this:
  /dev/hda1               /               ext2            noatime
0 0
  /dev/hda5               /boot           ext2            noauto,noatime
1 1
  /dev/hda6               /var            reiserfs        noatime
0 0
  /dev/hda7               /usr            reiserfs        noatime
0 0
  /dev/hda8               /opt            reiserfs        noatime
0 0
  /dev/hda9               /home           reiserfs        noatime
0 0
  /dev/hda10              none            swap            sw
0 0
  /dev/hdb1               none            swap            sw
q





> Is there a way to get it to boot so I can use the RAID to copy the data
> onto the new drives?
> 


>If you have access to all of your partitions this should not be
necessary. You are in "data recovery" mode. Unless you have a specific
reason for thinking for RAID it is often best left to the rebuilding
stage.


Yes, if the kernel you are booting from on the CD supports your RAID
controller (SCSI) or RAID IDE interface. Here's a link to the RAID FAQ
for help: http://www.faqs.org/contrib/linux-raid/x37.html


-Coop

reformatted them to get rid of the built in Windows-specific stuff and 
they work just fine. I also have a 1 GB Lexar Jump drive. They're 
actually a tad on the slow side; for transferring data between two 
machines, a CD-RW is often faster, including the erase.

Keith Lofstrom writes:

I used to have a "pretty slim form factor" drive, that "I never noticed
in my pocket".  It had a nasty disagreement with Mr. Washing Machine. 

Now I carry one of the little Iomega drives with the hinged cap.  This
guy is even smaller than my first drive, about 1.5 inches long.  It
fits in the little change pouch that I carry, and the change pouch is
big enough to always notice.  So that may be a clue, get a drive that
fits in something else that you always carry.  Hierarchy.

Both the previous thumb drive and this one "just work".  I mount mine
with "mount /flash".  You can also make this automatic.

From jeme at brelin.net  Thu Mar  3 13:13:52 2005

Subject: [PLUG] thumb drive recommendations?

Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503031310030.9474@shaft.bitmine.net>


On Wed, 2 Mar 2005, Elliott Mitchell wrote:
>> From: "Piet van Weel" <pmvw at wbcable.net>
>> I prefer the SanDisk Cruizer that takes the SD-Disk. The advantage is 
>> that I can upgrade the SD disk when a new one comes out. Perhaps this 
>> sounds fickle, but I've upgraded all the way from 32MB up to my current 
>> 256MB card!!
>>
>> Other USB type storage devices aren't upgradeable. They're disposable.
>
> I've got to wonder how much that is worth. Unless SD cards are the same 
> price or cheaper you're not saving by just replacing the card. I was 
> looking at ENU's web page, and didn't seem them listing SD at all.

There's more to consider than the purely monetary economic cost.  (And why 
do folks seem to always operate as if that one factor is the most 
important?)

You'd need to know whether the manufacture of SD cards consume more or 
less energy and materials and what sort of "externalities" are introduced 
by the production (pollution, subsidies, worker compensation, risk and 
living conditions, etc.) as compared to one-piece USB drives.  Then the 
disposable/upgradeable argument can have some concrete value.

J.

On Thu, 3 Mar 2005 10:00:14 -0700, Matt Alexander <lowbassman at gmail.com> wrote:
> I have the following in a shell script:
> 
> /usr/kerberos/bin/ftp -i -n -u <<EOF
> open ftp.somesite.com
> user someuser somepass
> pass
> mput somefiles*
> bye
> EOF
> 
> Is there a way to log all the information from the FTP transaction
> that you would normally see if this was done manually?
> Thanks,
> ~M

I do believe one method to do this is using script.

SCRIPT(1)
NAME
     script - make typescript of terminal session
DESCRIPTION
     script makes a typescript of everything printed on your terminal.

From michael at themontagnes.com  Fri Mar  4 16:50:07 2005

Subject: [PLUG] cron job won't run
Message-ID: <20050305005007.GA10380@themontagnes.com>

I have a cron job that calls a shell script shown below.  The rsync
commands don't seem to run.  I know the script runs cause the log file
at the end is correctly incremented.  Wonder what I've done wrong.
The same script runs correctly when called from the command line.

#!/bin/bash
rsync -Cavz --delete --exclude-from=exclude.txt mike at opsis:/Array/Office/General /store
rsync -Cavz --delete --exclude-from=exclude.txt mike at opsis:/Array/Office/Resource /store
rsync -Cavz --delete --exclude-from=exclude.txt mike at opsis:/Array/Marketing /home/backup
rsync -Cavz --delete --exclude-from=exclude.txt mike at opsis:/Array/Accounting /home/backup
echo `date` >> ~/backuplog.txt
scp ~/backuplog.txt mike at opsis:~

Michael Montagne
michael at themontagnes.com
http://www.themontagnes.com


From griffint at pobox.com  Fri Mar  4 17:02:57 2005
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Fri, 4 Mar 2005 17:02:57 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] cron job won't run
In-Reply-To: <20050305005007.GA10380@themontagnes.com>
References: <20050305005007.GA10380@themontagnes.com>
Message-ID: <20050305010257.GB27119@aracnet.com>

On Fri, Mar 04, 2005 at 04:50:07PM -0800, Michael Montagne wrote:
> I have a cron job that calls a shell script shown below.  The rsync
> commands don't seem to run.  I know the script runs cause the log file
> at the end is correctly incremented.  Wonder what I've done wrong.
> The same script runs correctly when called from the command line.
> 
> #!/bin/bash
> rsync -Cavz --delete --exclude-from=exclude.txt mike at opsis:/Array/Office/General /store
> rsync -Cavz --delete --exclude-from=exclude.txt mike at opsis:/Array/Office/Resource /store
> rsync -Cavz --delete --exclude-from=exclude.txt mike at opsis:/Array/Marketing /home/backup
> rsync -Cavz --delete --exclude-from=exclude.txt mike at opsis:/Array/Accounting /home/backup
> echo `date` >> ~/backuplog.txt
> scp ~/backuplog.txt mike at opsis:~
> 
>

Frequently this is due to something in your environment, or rather 
something that's missing from your cron job's environment. Try putting 
this line in your script:

   env > /tmp/my-cron-script.env

Let the cron job run then compare the contents of /tmp/my-cron-script.env 
to what you get when you run the env command from your shell prompt.

Terry
-- 
Terry Griffin <griffint at pobox.com>
http://www.blindchicken.com/~terryg/

there is a /bin/bask -k or -e options that you can put in the script
that echo everything back out.  I forget been a while since I debuged
a script.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Fri Mar  4 23:08:29 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Fri, 4 Mar 2005 23:08:29 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: cron job won't run
Message-ID: <20050305070829.GA10738@gate.kl-ic.com>


> Cron job that doesn't run ...

You should always run cron as if you have no environment, no path,
nothing.  So all commands should be sourced from root, for example:

/usr/bin/rsync -Cavz ...
... --exclude-from=/home/mike/exclude.txt ...
/usr/bin/scp ...
/bin/echo `/bin/date` >> ...

And always replace ~ with your full address.  It ain't /home/mike
if it ain't you runnin' it.  Or as Dorothy said, "there's no place
like home" :-)

Yes, sometimes cron knows.  But sometimes it knows the wrong thing;
it does not use your identical path or environment.  Never assume
anything about a script's environment (cron or otherwise), and it
will be more robust.

If the full path is too much typing, consider shell variables. 
Here are some you might define:

RSYNC='/usr/bin/rsync'
EXCLUDE='/home/mike/exclude.txt'                      # or wherever
RSYNCOPTS="-Cavz --delete --exclude-from=$EXCLUDE"
ARRAY='mike at opsis:Array'
TARGET='/home/backup'

... and your commands become

$RSYNC $RSYNCOPTS $ARRAY/Marketing  $TARGET
$RSYNC $RSYNCOPTS $ARRAY/Accounting $TARGET

Now it becomes easy to make this into a loop, for all your sources:

for source in Marketing Accounting
do
  $RSYNC $RSYNCOPTS $ARRAY/$source   $TARGET
done

You can do the same with echo, scp, date, etc...

Shell variables (near the start of the program) are Your Friends.
They save you a lot of retyping if something changes, or you decide
to use a different command or re-arrange your files.  If implemented
correctly, shell variables also allow you to radically change how
stuff works; for example, using a function that calls logger instead
of an scp to an over-written log file.  

- - -

Lastly, if you are doing backups, may I suggest you look at dirvish?
( www.dirvish.org )  It is a bit of overkill for what you are doing
now, but when you develop a full backup procedure, with history and
incrementals and security and file restores and such, you will find
dirvish much easier to maintain than re-inventing the wheel.  And
the upgrades are free!

Happy hacking!

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

If you can get past the advertising hype, the stuff at X10.com in the
camera section
is pretty good.  Sometimes you will see some of this stuff at Fry's
but mostly the
wired single camera systems. These systems with the receiver for wireless output
NTSC video.  Any BT848 video card should come up fine in linux with
the v4linux drivers
configured.  

I found an article in Linux Journal on "GNU motion*" that will
grab stuff from a v4linux device and only store images when things change.

http://www.lavrsen.dk/twiki/bin/view/Motion/WebHome

http://home.comcast.net/~rsteff.p/Pathfinder/index.html

In addition to a color camera that sends video to a receiver that outputs NTSC 
video, they also have a remote controlled pan/tilt head. I used two cameras 
in the activity (meant to give kids some sense of controlling a rover on 
Mars). One was mounted on the "rover" and one on the "lander." One of the 
pictures shows a couple of Commodore monitors with the video from the 
cameras. (Not the best photo, but the video is clean.)

There are 4 channels for the cameras. They operate in the same frequency space 
as one of the wireless ethernet systems (B, I think). The Portland State 
rocket guys use wireless ethernet to control their rocket, and we discovered 
that we were interfering with each other. By switching our cameras to 
channels 3 and 4, (or is it C & D?) it cleaned up the problem.

The cameras can run on battery, but you'd have to go out and replace them 
frequently, so for a security system, that's something of a problem. 
Otherwise, these should work.

These guys, 

http://www.smarthome.com/

have a lot of X10 stuff as well as other home security products. You mentioned 
a recorder: I don't know if it's what you had it mind, but they have time 
lapse recorders that will let you cram many hours onto a regular VHS tape.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens
http://home.comcast.net/~rsteff/

Note Cards & Photographic Prints avaliable at:
http://home.comcast.net/~rcsphoto/

From baloo at ursine.ca  Sat Mar  5 11:48:03 2005
From: baloo at ursine.ca (Paul Johnson)
Date: Sat, 5 Mar 2005 11:48:03 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] DVR security systems
In-Reply-To: <200503041844.21153.carla@bratgrrl.com>
References: <200503041844.21153.carla@bratgrrl.com>
Message-ID: <200503051148.05331.baloo@ursine.ca>

On Friday 04 March 2005 06:44 pm, Carla Schroder wrote:
> How much do you have to spend to get decent video quality?

Depends on if you're doing it for a webcam or security.  If you're going 
for security cameras, you're better off getting a standard security 
camera and a VCR.  If you actually have to use that footage to get a 
face or license plate from at a distance, whoever has to look at that 
footage will have nothing to zoom in on with a digital system 
(pixelated nature of digital pictures instantly obscures detail at a 
distance like a suspect on COPS).

On Fri, 2005-03-04 at 18:44 -0800, Carla Schroder wrote:
> I'm looking into installing a video security system, for outdoors, and after a

> night imaging. I have a couple of outbuildings to watch, so wireless would be 
> nice for them. The other two will be mounted on the outside of my house. I 
> think a DVR system is the way to go, but there are also some slick little 
> standalone units that might work for the outbuildings. 

I looked into this a couple of years ago, and the most versitale
solution I could come up with was network cameras.  Axis, www.axis.com
has a large variety of indoor and outdoor, some with pan/tilt and can be
powered through the ethernet cable.  The major advantage is that you
don't need a video capture device on the monitoring PC, just an network
connection.  This system is highly scalable and very easy to
(re)configure.  Wireless is nice, but you still have a power problem to
deal with.

At that time, Motion was just getting to the usable stage and from the
Linux Journal article I recently read, it looks like it has gotten more
robust and has more features.
> 
> I want to be able to record images and have some kind of portable playback, 
> like printing hard copies or copying to a CD or DVD.
> 
> Anyone have experience with these? Will an ordinary TV-enabled video card turn 
> a PC into a DVR?

This is all about the software, not the hardware.

>  How much do you have to spend to get decent video quality?

This, of course is relative, the more you spend the better the quality.
>  
> There's an awful lot of different options, and of course I don't want to 
> break the bank. Tips and useful links are welcome.

From carla at bratgrrl.com  Sat Mar  5 14:10:06 2005
From: carla at bratgrrl.com (Carla Schroder)
Date: Sat, 5 Mar 2005 14:10:06 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Wireless network
In-Reply-To: <20050305190950.40679.qmail@web60805.mail.yahoo.com>

On Saturday 05 March 2005 11:09 am, Ovid wrote:
> Hi all,
> 
> I'm running a computer with an FC2/Win2000 dual boot.  I need to set it
> up on my wireless network, but I don't know what sort of card would be
> good for FC2, or how to set it up for that matter.  Does anyone have
> any personal experience on good hardware I can look at that would be
> suitable?  
> 
> Internal or external.  I'm not picky.
> 
>

There are two ways to go wireless on Linux: easy, or excruciatingly painful. 
The pain comes from idiot hardware vendors changing their wireless chipsets 
every other day, almost always to some weird thing that is not supported in 
Linux. The easy way is to buy a Senao/EnGenius 2511 card, like this one with 
a built-in antenna:
http://www.netgate.com/product_info.php?cPath=26_39&products_id=42

The Senao card also comes in PCI, and can take an external antenna. It has 
about 7 times the transmitting power of most other PCI adapters, so you won't 
have a lot of dropped connections or slow speeds. Fedora should autodetect 
the card and load the correct drivers, all you have to do is enter your 
network configs. http://fedoranews.org/ is a good help resource.

These Linux Planet articles might be helpful:

Connecting to a Wireless LAN with Linux, Part 2
http://www.linuxplanet.com/linuxplanet/tutorials/5736/1/

 Connecting to a Wireless LAN with Linux, Part 1
http://www.linuxplanet.com/linuxplanet/tutorials/5728/1/

to be useful.

It won't work as an AP, but I can 
get it to work for ad-hoc 
connections.

Without even orienting the antenna 
in the right direction, I know I 
can reach at least one place worth 
getting to.  I'm sure I can do a 
long range wireless network even 
if I have to do multiple hops.  
I don't know how to activate WEP. 
There's something called WPA 
also.  I'm using the Windows XP 
driver from RealTek's webiste 
with ndiswrapper-1.0, 
Slackware-10.1, and a 2.6.10 kernel.

One gotcha is that you must compile 
usb support as a module and modules 
for usb hub support seem to be needed 
as well.  My wifi adapter isn't USB 
based, but ndiswrapper probably 
requires USB hooks in the kernel
for other wireless adapters that 
are.

NFS root with Slackware-10.1 is a 
cinch.  All I had to do was add a 
single if in rc.S to 
bypass the file system check and 
voila.  I wish I knew how to turn 
hotplug support off.  I don't 
have anything in my router box 
that needs that.  The way the
the Slackware 10.1 modutils
work with both 2.4 and 2.6
kernels is sweet.

I can run these cards in ad-hoc 
mode.  I don't know if ndiswrapper 
with the most recent XP driver 
can operate the card as an access 
point, but I can at least establish 
point to point links now.

From plug_0 at robinson-west.com  Sat Mar  5 20:55:59 2005
From: plug_0 at robinson-west.com (plug_0 at robinson-west.com)
Date: Sat,  5 Mar 2005 20:55:59 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Wireless network
In-Reply-To: <20050305190950.40679.qmail@web60805.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20050305190950.40679.qmail@web60805.mail.yahoo.com>

Quoting Ovid <publiustemp-plug at yahoo.com>:

> Hi all,
> 
> I'm running a computer with an FC2/Win2000 dual boot.  I need to set it
> up on my wireless network, but I don't know what sort of card would be

> 
> Internal or external.  I'm not picky.
> 
> Cheers,
> Ovid
> 
> If this message is a response to a question on a mailing list, please send
> follow up questions to the list.
> 
> Web Programming with Perl -- http://users.easystreet.com/ovid/cgi_course/
> _______________________________________________
> PLUG mailing list
> PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
> http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug

On any 2.6 based Linux system ndiswrapper 1.0 will support Realtek 
8180 chipset cards using the Windows XP driver.  The best cards to 
get are Orinoco Classic Gold and Prism based adapters.  Any PCI 
based PC card adapter should work for a standup.  

Orinoco and the like are better because there are open source 
drivers and if I'm not mistaken, you can build access points 
using these adapters.

If you need antennas, check out http://www.etherdesigns.com/

The important thing is to search google for success stories 
before buying a wireless card.  Don't just go for something 
the minute there's any mention of opeability with Linux, 
find comments on Slashdot etc.  Watch out for cards that use
proprietary Linux drivers which don't work well or at all.

     Michael Robinson

I recently bought a Gateway WBM-120; I got it for $10 on eBay.  It's a
rebranded GemTek card, which uses a Prism chipset and works fine on FC3
after adding the card IDs to the PCMCIA config (see http://nakedape.cc/wiki
for full details).

That said, I'm told the Lucent Golds are on sale at Fry's for about $25.

readable! When I first got it, I went web surfing, only to discover that 
Sharp had de-commissioned it as a consumer product with that sort of 
support, and all the hacker sites had only stuff for the 5500 or the 
Japanese clamshell versions. So ... mine is idle too, although if I had 
a pair of them I could at least have one virgin and one crash-and-burn, 
connected by infrared. :)

I was just reading the info for gimp (rpm -qi gimp) and I noticed that
they recommend installing a couple of packages of fonts,
ftp.gimp.org/pub/gimp/fonts/freefonts-0.10.tar.gz
and
ftp.gimp.org/pub/gimp/fonts/sharefonts-0.10.tar.gz
The README file in freefonts-0.10.tar.gz says to cd
to  /usr/X11/lib/fonts and untar.  On my Fedora 3 system, I think this
is equivalent to /usr/X11R6/lib/X11/fonts, which contains a lot of
subdirs: 100dpi  75dpi  CID  OTF  Speedo  TTF  Type1  encodings  local
misc  util.  After untarring, there would be a new directory freefonts.

I'm concerned that this advice may be out of date.  Does any  gimp user
know whether installing these fonts this way works or is beneficial or
is unnecessay?

From plug_0 at robinson-west.com  Tue Mar  8 01:44:13 2005
From: plug_0 at robinson-west.com (plug_0 at robinson-west.com)
Date: Tue, 8 Mar 2005 01:44:13 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Encrypting email...
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0503080024450.13597-100000@goose.robinson-west.com>

I've had a problem with unauthorized access of a 
Horde IMP accessible email account.  I'm curious 
about encrypting the messages in the account so 
that an individual who intercepts them is far 
less likely to know their content.  In essence,
I want someone who figures out the password
to only get garbage if they don't know the
decryption secret.

Lately, this person and I have agreed to cease 
communicating for a decent length of time hoping 
to discourage the thief.

I've learned that the password was known by 
the thief.  The old password, pocahontas,
was too simple.  Then again, it wasn't like
anyone was supposed to know this email 
account existed for her and I didn't expect
anyone to guess the password.  I didn't
notice any failed logins, so I don't think
this person ever had to guess.

At this point, I've limited remote 
logins by ip and I changed the 
password.  Unfortunately, this 
person has said that he/she can 
figure out the password regardless 
of what it's set to.

I have a feeling her ISP based email
accounts will be hacked or via 
some clever dishonesty gotten into.
Oh well.  I suppose she can give 
email up completely except for safe 
messages that she has to send.

I realize encryption isn't a solution,
but it could at least slow the thief.  
If it slows the thief enough, 
maybe my friend and I can 
communicate again in this way.  
There's a telephone, but when it is 
used there is an easily obtained 
record of the call.  If I had known
the password was going to leak, I
might have declared a communication
blackout months ago.

For starters, I'm thinking I can encrypt 
messages by mapping the alphabet to a 
different set of 26 symbols.  I figure 
I can start with a mixture of numbers 
and letters.  I would be nice if I had 
a program I can email to that will
encrypt the message and then forward
it on to her account.  I figure if I
have five different mappings and 
a random one is used for each paragraph
in an email, that that should be 
reasonably hard to crack.  Maybe some
letters should be replaced with two
symbols so that a cracker doesn't
know the length of the original
word.  If I have say nine symbols
to replace spaces with and I use
them randomly, it should be very 
hard to decipher the message.



From russj at dimstar.net  Wed Mar  9 14:44:54 2005
From: russj at dimstar.net (Russ Johnson)
Date: Wed, 09 Mar 2005 14:44:54 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Encrypting email...
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0503080024450.13597-100000@goose.robinson-west.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0503080024450.13597-100000@goose.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <422F7C66.5020104@dimstar.net>

plug_0 at robinson-west.com wrote:

>I've had a problem with unauthorized access of a 
>Horde IMP accessible email account.
>
(TONS of extra fluff deleted. Leave out the extra stuff, just ask the 
pertinent questions. We don't care about your private life. This will 
also make your posts much shorter and easier to decypher.)

First question...

Is the email accessible through the web?

If yes, do you encrypt that connection?

If no, then there's your hole. A packet sniffer will reveal the password.

The same holds true for pop3 and imap. If the connections aren't 
encrypted, the password is in cleartext.

Russ

> If no, then there's your hole. A packet sniffer will reveal the password.

And encryption is moot if the client machine has a keylogger installed
on it, as is common on windows machines.

There's a number of ways the user's password could have been compromised
without requiring any guessing on the part of the attacker, from sticky
notes to using the same known password from another compromised email
account.

From znmeb at cesmail.net  Wed Mar  9 19:43:41 2005
From: znmeb at cesmail.net (M. Edward (Ed) Borasky)
Date: Wed, 09 Mar 2005 19:43:41 -0800

plug_0 at robinson-west.com wrote:

>I've tried gentoo, but I admittedly haven't been very impressed
>with it thus far.
>
>I'd say it's for experts because you can't willy nilly
>set the use flags.  I imagine there are some secrets
>to getting everything working.  Then again, I installed
>on a Dell laptop where laptops notorious for being
>slightly incompatible with Linux.
>  
>
The secret to USE flags is to stick with the defaults at first, then 
modify them and re-emerge as features are needed. Actually, Portage has 
a recent addition, "emerge --newuse world", which rebuilds anything that 
needs rebuilding because a USE flag changed.

>In theory being forced to compile everything is an interesting 
>idea, but from a practical standpoint I'd have to say that
>gentoo has quite a way to go before binary based Linux
>distributions will be a thing of the past.
>  
>
I would agree if the binary distros would standardize (for x86) on i686 
compilation. I have three machines -- a P3, an Athlon XP and an Athlon 
Tbird, and I find i686 compilation acceptable except for 
numeric-intensive code like R. That way I can have a common package 
repository and not have to recompile as often.

From plug at merlot.com  Thu Mar 10 09:14:26 2005
From: plug at merlot.com (Kurt Sussman)
Date: Thu, 10 Mar 2005 09:14:26 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Listing only directory names
In-Reply-To: <863bv3qvo1.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503100851420.28227@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<863bv3qvo1.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <20050310171426.GB12920@merlot.com>

Russell Senior (seniorr at aracnet.com) typed this ...
> >>>>> "Rich" == Rich Shepard <rshepard at appl-ecosys.com> writes:
> 
> Rich>    What is the shell solution to listing only subdirectories
> Rich> within a directory?
> 
>   $ find . -type d

Or to list only the current directory (not all directories from the
start down):

 $ find . -type d -maxdepth 1

And to get a more detailed listing of the directories:

 $ find . -type d -maxdepth 1 | xargs ls -l 

--Kurt

From steve at wirex.net  Thu Mar 10 09:41:10 2005
From: steve at wirex.net (Steve Beattie)
Date: Thu, 10 Mar 2005 09:41:10 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Listing only directory names
In-Reply-To: <20050310171426.GB12920@merlot.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503100851420.28227@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
	<863bv3qvo1.fsf@coulee.tdb.com> <20050310171426.GB12920@merlot.com>
Message-ID: <20050310174110.GA15460@wirex.net>

On Thu, Mar 10, 2005 at 09:14:26AM -0800, Kurt Sussman wrote:
> Or to list only the current directory (not all directories from the
> start down):
> 
>  $ find . -type d -maxdepth 1
> 
> And to get a more detailed listing of the directories:
> 
>  $ find . -type d -maxdepth 1 | xargs ls -l 

gnu find (and others, I recall solaris find supporting it as well)
support the -ls argument, so you can do:

  find . -type d -maxdepth 1 -ls 

to see the attribute information on the directories themselves (-ls is
the equivalent of 'ls -dils' according to the manpage).

From hapibeli at comcast.net  Thu Mar 10 21:27:19 2005

Since installing Fedora Core 3, I've had no sound, yet this same box
uses the Creative EMU 0404 and the Creative SB Live soundcards to great
effect when I boot into the Win XP hdd on the same box. I'm using the
ccrma.stanford.edu fedora/3/i386 release as I'm planning on some music
editing.I've run alsaconf and Alsa sees the onboard AC 97 sound, which I

Live soundcard, but NO sound.
Can someone guide me to the noise?

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Thu Mar 10 22:40:22 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Thu, 10 Mar 2005 22:40:22 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Sound FC3
In-Reply-To: <1110518839.5230.28.camel@localhost.localdomain>
References: <1110518839.5230.28.camel@localhost.localdomain>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503102216520.9636@localhost>

Sounds like a kernel config issue.  Build a new kernel with the options
customized for your hardware.  Use lspci and cat /proc/cpuinfo to find
out what all the hardware is.

If you are running a stock distro kernel, it is sure to be bloated
beyond reason with completely unnecessary drivers.  This increases the
risk of conflicts.  It also eats up RAM for no reason (at least the
compiled-in code does).

Go to /usr/src/linux as root and run "make menuconfig", and browse
around Device Drivers -> Sound.  If it won't start, make sure your
config file (/boot/config<something>) is copied to
/usr/src/linux/.config .

Also run lsmod to see if you have any sound modules loaded.  You almost
never see stock kernels with these drivers compiled into the kernel,
therefore they would show up here.

Sometimes you'll be sure that you're tweaking the right config option,
but it won't work.  Those situations call for a bit of trial and error
with compiling the option into the bzImage vs. compiling it as a kernel
module.  Sometimes conflicts can be circumvented this way.  I had this
happen once recently - with alsa drivers!  I absolutely had to compile
my sound driver as a module.  Not my favorite setup - I like everything
that I'll ALWAYS want up and running compiled into the kernel, so I
won't be down if module loading breaks.

Throw in a knoppix disk and see if sound works when booted up under it.
Choose the 2.6 kernel at boot time by typing "knoppix26".  If
sound works under knoppix, run lsmod and compare to your FC3 list.

Adjust /etc/modules to look for the right modules to load at system init
time.  Maybe fedora has a module-management mechanism?  I don't know - I
use a well-seasoned knoppix load that's been passed around a bit.
Knoppix does have a module list management feature.  On my machine, I
would modify /etc/modules_<kernel_version> instead of the actual
/etc/modules file, because knoppix has a startup script that finds the
/etc/modules<kernel_version> variant that matches your current kernel
version, and copies that file to /etc/modules.  So /etc/modules gets
overwritten at every boot.  It goes along with their dual-kernel CDs,
where you have a choice between a 2.4 or a 2.6 kernel.  The 2 kernels
have different module requirements, and the same modules have different
names.  Anyway, be on the lookout for that kind of thing on fedira.

Sometimes th problem is just that the sound is muted. 
Run alsamixer and make sure that the volume is turned
up and not muted. If that is not the problem then the
correct modules are not being loaded.

Bill Barry

From griffint at pobox.com  Fri Mar 11 07:02:36 2005
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Fri, 11 Mar 2005 07:02:36 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Sound FC3
In-Reply-To: <1110518839.5230.28.camel@localhost.localdomain>
References: <1110518839.5230.28.camel@localhost.localdomain>
Message-ID: <200503110702.37087.griffint@pobox.com>

On Thursday 10 March 2005 9:27 pm, Dirk Ouellette wrote:
> Since installing Fedora Core 3, I've had no sound, yet this same box
> uses the Creative EMU 0404 and the Creative SB Live soundcards to great
> effect when I boot into the Win XP hdd on the same box. I'm using the
> ccrma.stanford.edu fedora/3/i386 release as I'm planning on some music
> editing.I've run alsaconf and Alsa sees the onboard AC 97 sound, which I
> don't care about, and it says that I've got the alsamixer set for the SB
> Live soundcard, but NO sound.
> Can someone guide me to the noise?
> Thanks
>

This is a known problem in FC3 with a large number (but not all) sound
chips. I can happen in FC2 as well if you upgrade to a 2.6.10 kernel.

The basic problem (at least for my chips) is that certain mixer settings
are not getting set to sensible defaults. And even if you finally get
them set correctly yourself, an actl save/restore cycle (as when rebooting)
doesn't restore them correctly.

You can usually get it to work just by finding that mystery mixer setting
that's getting in the way. For the chip on my laptop it's the mixer's DAC
switch. On my HTPC it's the input capture selector.

Terry

From redhat at crisponions.com  Fri Mar 11 07:51:56 2005
From: redhat at crisponions.com (Len Icks)
Date: Fri, 11 Mar 2005 07:51:56 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Sound FC3
Message-ID: <CC5738F2CE677746976EC06CBD6B9D98013F1C@toonces.crisponions.com>

I had this exact same set up and had the same problem, I ended up
pulling the emu card before I found the fix, but it turned out that the
mixer (I use Kmix) had set my SB card to use digital out as the default,
I changed that to analog and the problem was fixed.

Dave

From mikeraz at patch.com  Fri Mar 11 12:44:19 2005
From: mikeraz at patch.com (Michael Rasmussen)
Date: Fri, 11 Mar 2005 12:44:19 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] vim versus the clipboard - found a solution
In-Reply-To: <20050223205029.35721.qmail@web60806.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20050223205029.35721.qmail@web60806.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20050311204419.GA15781@patch.com>

Ovid wrote:
> I am editing a bunch of files in vim and I need to paste the contents
> into an HTML text area.
> ... to copy the current buffer contents, but that doesn't work when I'm
> using vim in a terminal window.  I thought the "*" buffer would work,
> but it doesn't seem to.  How can I copy the current vim buffer file
> contents to the clipboard (on Fedora Core 2)?

In the Linux Journal weekly reader this week there was a reference to a utility called
xsel. It does just what you're asking.

There's a debian package for unstable, for everyone else there's a tgz that compiles
and installs very quickly.

  http://www.vergenet.net/~conrad/software/xsel/

For Ovid's original need one can edit away in vi and then:

  :%!xsel

and then middle click in the HTML text area for a paste. 
  WARNING
This will cause an effective cut of the buffer contents so you'll need to follow up 
with a `u` to undo the command. 

The LJ snip about the utility:

  Tech Tip

   Want to write a shell script that works with the user's selected text
   from a different X application? Use xsel. For example, you can count
   the number of words in the selected text with

xsel -o | wc -w

   Other command-line options are available to get and set the X
   "clipboard" and the little-used "secondary selection", too. For more
   information, check out the xsel Web site:
   http://www.vergenet.net/~conrad/software/xsel/ and X Selections, Cut
   Buffers and Kill Rings:
   http://www.jwz.org/doc/x-cut-and-paste.html .



-- 
    Michael Rasmussen, Portland Oregon  
  Be appropriate && Follow your curiosity
 http://meme.patch.com/memes/BicycleRiding
   Get Fixed:  http://www.dampfixie.org

	n = ((n >>  1) & 0x55555555) | ((n <<  1) & 0xaaaaaaaa);
	n = ((n >>  2) & 0x33333333) | ((n <<  2) & 0xcccccccc);
	n = ((n >>  4) & 0x0f0f0f0f) | ((n <<  4) & 0xf0f0f0f0);
	n = ((n >>  8) & 0x00ff00ff) | ((n <<  8) & 0xff00ff00);
	n = ((n >> 16) & 0x0000ffff) | ((n << 16) & 0xffff0000);

		-- C code which reverses the bits in a word.



From cstevens at gencom.us  Fri Mar 11 15:21:47 2005

Subject: [PLUG] PC Garage Sale

All,

I was just handed a 400 MHz. Machine for free. Now, the truth is that I
have more machines than I know what to do with. I said that I would
probably give the machine away to FreeGeek or other such charity.

Then the thought occured to me that there are likely others in the same
boat: one too many boxes but no real avenue to get rid of it and at the
same time make a little change.

So I just thought of the idea of having a kind of PC garage sale. I
recall an article on the net that talks about doing this. An example of
organization is using different colors of stickers to identify each
sale.

The house could take, say, 10 per cent of the cut for a working
computer. For that the house can clean the computer and even perhaps
install Linux on it. This helps create value for the computer.

Let's do this!


-Coop

Terry Griffin wrote:

>On Thursday 10 March 2005 9:27 pm, Dirk Ouellette wrote:
>  
>
>>Since installing Fedora Core 3, I've had no sound, yet this same box
>>uses the Creative EMU 0404 and the Creative SB Live soundcards to great
>>effect when I boot into the Win XP hdd on the same box. I'm using the
>>ccrma.stanford.edu fedora/3/i386 release as I'm planning on some music
>>editing.I've run alsaconf and Alsa sees the onboard AC 97 sound, which I
>>don't care about, and it says that I've got the alsamixer set for the SB
>>Live soundcard, but NO sound.
>>Can someone guide me to the noise?
>>Thanks
>>
>>    
>>
>
>This is a known problem in FC3 with a large number (but not all) sound
>chips. I can happen in FC2 as well if you upgrade to a 2.6.10 kernel.
>
>The basic problem (at least for my chips) is that certain mixer settings
>are not getting set to sensible defaults. And even if you finally get
>them set correctly yourself, an actl save/restore cycle (as when rebooting)
>doesn't restore them correctly.
>
>You can usually get it to work just by finding that mystery mixer setting
>that's getting in the way. For the chip on my laptop it's the mixer's DAC
>switch. On my HTPC it's the input capture selector.
>
>Terry
>_______________________________________________
>PLUG mailing list
>PLUG at lists.pdxlinux.org
>http://lists.pdxlinux.org/mailman/listinfo/plug
>
>  
>
I've got a similar problem -- Gentoo has no problem sounding off but FC3 
is silent on the same box. Maybe if I bring Gentoo up, write down the 
mixer settings, then install them in FC3, the sound will work.

From heinlein at madboa.com  Mon Mar 14 10:28:38 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Mon, 14 Mar 2005 10:28:38 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Extract Google referrals from Apache logs
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.62.0503141016530.3304@arrowhead.galois.com>

I wanted a fast/easy way to get a summary of what Google queries are 
landing people on what pages. The script below is the result. It 
expects an Apache log as STDIN.

My Perl skills are a bit rusty these days, so feel free to suggest 
improvements.

--Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

#!/usr/bin/perl -w

use strict;
use CGI;

while ( <> ) {
   chomp;
   # parse log entries
   m/^
     (\S+)\s+           # remote address or hostname
     (\S+)\s+(\S+)\s+   # user and group
     \[([^\]]+)\]\s+    # date and time
     "([^"]+)"\s+       # request, parsed later
     (\d+)\s+(\S+)\s+   # http status code and number of bytes sent
     "([^"]+)"\s+       # referring url
     "([^"]+)"          # user agent
     $
   /x;

   # assign matches
   my ($addr, $user, $group, $time, $req, $status, $bytes, $ref, $agent) =
      ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5, $6, $7, $8, $9);

   # let CGI.pm parse the referrer string
   my $q = CGI->new($ref);
   my $query = $q->param('q') or next;

   # this should always return a good value...
   my $page = $1 if $req =~ m/^\S+\s+(\S+)/;

   # report findings
   print "Search query:  ", $q->param('q'), "\n";
   print "Page accessed: ", $page, "\n\n";

}

Those protocols are used by IPSec. File /etc/protocols describes
them as:

esp     50      ESP             # encapsulating security payload
ah      51      AH              # authentication header

I did a quick Google search on:  A76 S76 battery life
gave website me this insight.
http://www.photoethnography.com/ClassicCameras/index-frameset.html?batteries.html~mainFrame 
A= alkaline S=silver oxide 
He says the alkaline doesn't last as long.  Lifetime is a big deal for cameras, and 
equipment that you depend on to work.

This cross reference is good too:  http://www.butkus.org/chinon/duracell_battery.htm 

This is type of info is helpful for HP calculator users. 
There are many similar sounding and lower priced batteries that don't have similar life.



From max.reid at saikonetworks.com  Mon Mar 14 16:11:50 2005
From: max.reid at saikonetworks.com (max.reid at saikonetworks.com)
Date: Mon, 14 Mar 2005 16:11:50 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] iptables and protocol 50 and 51
In-Reply-To: <20050314230644.GA21716@aracnet.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0503141327560.21013-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
	<20050314230644.GA21716@aracnet.com>
Message-ID: <1110845510.42362846485c5@webmail.no-ip.com>


Just to clarify, these are IP protcols, not TCP and UDP "port" numbers.  

Protocol 50 is Encapsulated Security Payload, which provides for both encryption
and authentication, AH just provides authentication.  Most folks only use ESP.

This is similar to OSPF being IP protocol 89, EIGRP 88 etc.

Regards,
Max

>

Is it a managed switch that you can get port stats from?
At work I've seen this frequently when a client can't support the
full duplex.  We'll see sky high error counts on the port. 

Forcing the client to 100/half solves the problem and dramatically
increase throughput.

# The following was supposedly scribed by
# Jeme A Brelin
# on Monday 14 March 2005 10:13 pm:

>So, I've got two relatively unloaded hosts running no other network
>applications through a mostly unused switch on my home network.
>
>Current FTP transfer speeds seem to be around 8KBps.

That's 64Kbps right? (1B=8b)  Remember, 100Mb is the theoretical speed 
for raw bits.  If you're measuring the size of transferred files vs 
time, you're not counting the TCP packet overhead, etc.

I usually test with wget, and have seen anywhere from 3-11 MB/s 
depending on the speed of the machine and quality of the network card.  
The tulip and eepro100 cards seem to perform better than some.

What's your machine spec and card setup?

> applications through a mostly unused switch on my home network.

Waow.  You've got a few things that could be causing it:
2 interrupt controllers, 2 IP stacks, 2 drivers, 2 NICs, 2 cables, 
2 switch ports, 1 switch backplane.

To me, that order of degradation while still maintaining a connection
implies something on the interrupt, driver or software side.
It'd be interesting to try each host from another machine, and/or
retest with one host or the other booted from a LiveCD.

Heck, maybe someone installed bandwidth-limiting as a gag. ;)

On 2005-03-15, Michael Rasmussen <mikeraz at patch.com> wrote:
> Jeme A Brelin wrote:
>> So, I've got two relatively unloaded hosts running no other network 
>> applications through a mostly unused switch on my home network.
>> 
>> Current FTP transfer speeds seem to be around 8KBps.
>> 
>> How the hell?
>
> Is it a managed switch that you can get port stats from?
> At work I've seen this frequently when a client can't support the
> full duplex.  We'll see sky high error counts on the port. 
>
> Forcing the client to 100/half solves the problem and dramatically
> increase throughput.

You can, of course, try forcing it to full too :) I've had recommendations
from admins of larger Ethernet networks to generally fix the speed and
duplexity servers and such, because (supposedly) the renegotiation incurs
some overhead, which you might notice doing backups or such.

'mii-tool' is the way to go if the driver supports it; if not, the
module itself will require options.

Wil

From rich at paranoid.org  Mon Mar 14 22:07:31 2005
From: rich at paranoid.org (Rich Burroughs)
Date: Mon, 14 Mar 2005 22:07:31 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: Slowest Full duplex 100MB in the west
In-Reply-To: <slrnd3cqe6.3oq.wcooley@rheingold.nakedape.priv>

	<slrnd3cqe6.3oq.wcooley@rheingold.nakedape.priv>
Message-ID: <42367BA3.5040809@paranoid.org>

Wil Cooley wrote:

> You can, of course, try forcing it to full too :) I've had recommendations
> from admins of larger Ethernet networks to generally fix the speed and
> duplexity servers and such, because (supposedly) the renegotiation incurs
> some overhead, which you might notice doing backups or such.

I've run into this before with Sun boxes and Cisco switches. The 
performance would be pretty bad if you had the switch set to 
autonegotiate, but it worked fine if you set it to full duplex. I think 
it is best in general to choose the settings you want instead of relying 
on the autonegotiation.


Rich




From srau at rauhaus.org  Mon Mar 14 22:36:05 2005
From: srau at rauhaus.org (Stafford A. Rau)
Date: Mon, 14 Mar 2005 22:36:05 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Slowest Full duplex 100MB in the west
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503142058190.22246@shaft.bitmine.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503142012011.22246@shaft.bitmine.net>
	<20050315044659.GJ21325@bavariati.org>
	<Pine.LNX.4.61.0503142058190.22246@shaft.bitmine.net>
Message-ID: <20050315063605.GA1721@rauhaus.org>

* Jeme A Brelin <jeme at brelin.net> [050314 21:01]:
> 
> jbrelin at robot:~# ifconfig eth0
> eth0      Link encap:Ethernet  HWaddr 00:A0:CC:E5:A5:34
>           inet addr:10.42.42.41  Bcast:10.42.42.255  Mask:255.255.255.0
>           UP BROADCAST RUNNING MULTICAST  MTU:1500  Metric:1
>           RX packets:8794083 errors:42726 dropped:0 overruns:0 frame:63831
>           TX packets:10335895 errors:4 dropped:0 overruns:1 carrier:3
 
> Doesn't appear to be errors... unless it's a single digit tally in mod 5.

You seem to have a lot of receive errors on robot's eth0. Speed/duplex
mismatch between the switch and host, as mentioned previously, is the
likely culprit.

Autonegotiation only works if both ends are set to autonegotiate - if
you have one end forced to, for instance, 100MB/Full duplex, and the
other end set to autonegotiate, the end set to auto will drop to half
duplex and you will get errors.

Best to force both ends to match speed and duplex, but if you want
autonegotiation to work, then both ends need to be auto.

--Stafford

trigger the problem.

force the client to auto, then 100/full, then 100/half and test
the throughput under each scenario.

Ronald Chmara wrote:
> >>>>         RX packets:8794083 errors:42726 dropped:0 overruns:0
> >>>>frame:63831
> >>>------------------------------>^^^^^^^^^^^^
> >>That's not enough to cause the level of losses you were talking
> >>about....
> >Sure it is, if the errors occured during the ftp process.
> 
> 'splain, please. That's only 0.4 percent of packets, so unless each bad 

We don't know how long the interface has been up and what percentage of 
total the ftp traffic is.  Of the 8794083 packets received perhaps
1% of them were the ftp traffic that Jeme's describing, perhaps 50%.
We don't know.  Thus he needs to test.  OR he could grab the interface
statistics before and after an FTP transfer - we could then see how
the numbers have incremented. We might see something like the RX packets
growing by 1000 while the error count grew by several hundred.

You'll also note that he has frame errors.  Frame errors are when the
received packet has a bad CRC and/or non-integer number of octets. 
These are usually the result of collisions or bad Ethernet device.  


> seeing how it would drop a 100Mb/s to 8KB/s. Maybe 100Mb/s 
> (theoretical) to 30 Mb/s (actual), but 64 Kb/s? Roughly five hundred 
> times slower?

I've seen it on workstations at work - less than T1 speeds on a 100mhz
LAN connection.  Setting the duplex on both ends of the connection, 
in our case to half, restored expected transfer rates.  Setting to full
did not.  I suspect this is due to the quality of the Ethernet chipset
used in the low cost desktop machines we have. But it hasn't been worth
spending the time to investigate.

Jeme's situation, and that of most home users, is a bit trickier because
he/they don't have managed switches.  The typical home Ethernet switch
is auto-sensing and the user has no way to set port parameters 
or view port statistics. 

> I'd guess crappy cables, or *serious* interference, or 
> something similar on the physical layer...

That could well be, that's for the person on site to evaluate.

From max.reid at saikonetworks.com  Tue Mar 15 09:00:40 2005
From: max.reid at saikonetworks.com (max.reid at saikonetworks.com)

Subject: [PLUG] Slowest Full duplex 100MB in the west

	<6abefb61859414625b04bb7ecf28f99f@opus1.com>
	<20050315101201.GC7246@patch.com>
	<3c70499f8b79e1bd16dd94da83347e97@opus1.com>
Message-ID: <1110906040.423714b8eeaed@webmail.no-ip.com>



1) 100 Half will in many cases provide worse performance than 10 Half.  Speed
and duplex are definately the first thing you want to correct, if possible.  The
most common way to correct this is to set the duplex negotiation to auto on both
the switch and client.

2) Have we tried to benchmark throughput using another application, like HTTP?
Bittorent, NFS? 

3) Ethereal is your friend.  take a capture and run it through Shane Ostermann's
tcptrace application.  It will breakdown the TCP level dynamics, showing packet
loss and retransmissions, etc.

HTH.

Regards,
Max

> Fired up a flick on the XBox.  No errors.  Nothing but smooth transfers.
>
>> You'll also note that he has frame errors.  Frame errors are when the 
>> received packet has a bad CRC and/or non-integer number of octets. 
>> These are usually the result of collisions or bad Ethernet device.
>
>
> I really WANT to blame my crappy switch (so I can justify buying a new 
> one), but I'm not seeing ANY errors on my new desktop machine or 
> transfers between other hosts.

> Dig this.  400KBps.  No way to check interface errors on the XBox, but 
> my guess is that we will find few to none with a transfer rate like 
> that. (Still slow, though... the switch lights green or orange 
> depending on whether the interface is 10 or 100Mb and the XBox is 
> orange.  I replaced my last internal green-lit card last week.)
>
>> Jeme's situation, and that of most home users, is a bit trickier 
>> because he/they don't have managed switches.  The typical home 
>> Ethernet switch is auto-sensing and the user has no way to set port 
>> parameters or view port statistics.
>
>
> And managed switches are really expensive.
>
>>> I'd guess crappy cables, or *serious* interference, or
>>> something similar on the physical layer...
>>
>>
>> That could well be, that's for the person on site to evaluate.
>
>
> I'm more inclined to think it's the switch or the NIC than the cables, 
> but only because I would think the cables would munge data regardless 
> of transfer speed.
>
A couple of years ago, I had an ethernet switch/hub (built into a IDSL 
router) fail
in a peculiar manner.  Small frames worked just fine.  I could 
ping/traceroute all
day long without error ... until I started to increment the packet 
size.  POP3 users
accessing small messages didn't even notice a problem ... those who had mail
messages over a few K (esp. those w/ multi-meg PDF, etc.), or were trying to
use an FTP server on the same segment were completely shutdown.

First, make sure you have a quick test which reliably reproduces the 
problem.
(And it sounds like your FTP test is working well.)

Then, the quickest (and cheapest), thing to try is to use a different 
port on the
switch.  (For that matter, what happens if the "robot" and "person" 
ports are
swapped?)  You may just have a bad port, and I've seen more than a few
engineering/lab nets with red tape covering blown ports....

Second, swap out the cable ...  again, fast, cheap.

Next, you get to decide if you want to swap out (a) the switch, or (b) 
the NIC.
....

Portland Linux/Unix Group Advanced Topics

Speaker:            Alan Olsen
                    
Subject:            Redhat Package Manager - How to roll your own packages

Date:               March 16th 2005
Time:               7:00pm - 9:00pm

Location:           Jax 826 SW 2nd Ave
                    Portland, OR

The talk will be on how to create RPMs for Linux systems and any other
OSes that use the Redhat Package Manager. (Redhat, Fedora, SuSE,
Mandrake, etc.)  The talk will include how to create a spec file,
determine dependencies, and make everything work without pulling out too
much of your hair.

We will not be getting into why RPM is better than Debian's package
manager, though some aspects of package are fairly universal. (APT and
YUM will get some mention, but they are not package managers so much as
installers.)

Usual meeting rules apply. Happy Hour meal prices for the first hour.

From creswick at gmail.com  Mon Mar 14 12:06:29 2005

Subject: [PLUG] Ethernet cable test devices
In-Reply-To: <4231CB4A.9030000@aracnet.com>

Message-ID: <c834ec805031412063d2deb36@mail.gmail.com>

On Fri, 11 Mar 2005 08:46:02 -0800, Maodhog <techmage at aracnet.com> wrote: 
> I'm looking at Siemons and Fluke and a device from Trendware(?) but it's
> really just to let me know when I've screwed up building a cable(crossed
> wires or when the roll-over is wired as a cross-over). I came to this
> conclusion of need when it took me thirty tries to get one roll-over
> correctly.


If all you want to check is that your wires are straigh or crossed as
they should be, and you aren't concerned with the internal
capabilities of the strands so much you can use any hub with a uplink
port and lights.

Plug one end into the uplink and the other into a standard port, if
the lights turn on you've at least got connectivity.  Use both
standard ports for crossovers.

Obviously this isn't good enough for any serious validation of your
cables, but I'm not sure how complex you want to go.

-Rogan

I played around with mii-tool for quite a bit and found that the responses 
were... inconsistent.  It wouldn't, for example, be forced into any mode 
at all and whenever I narrowed the advertised media, it negotiated 
10/half (at which time the light on the switch turned from amber meaning 
100 to green meaning 10).  Under certain conditions, the card would just 
say "unable to negotiate" and then I'd have no link at all.

$15 later, I have a new nic and ftp transfers are in a more acceptable 
13MiB range.

Bad NIC bad, new NIC good.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Wed Mar 16 06:50:28 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Wed, 16 Mar 2005 06:50:28 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Re: Bad Ethernet Cables (was  Re: Slowest Full duplex ...)
In-Reply-To: <20050316084545.308EA424B@ulke.nakedape.cc>
References: <20050316084545.308EA424B@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <20050316145028.GA29665@gate.kl-ic.com>


On Tue, 15 Mar 2005, keith morse wrote:
> Don't discount one of the ethernet cables being flakey either.

Jeme A Brelin wrote:
> Oddly, I can't find a decent cable with which to test, but I did mentally 
> discount cable issues because lower speed transfer rates work great.  The 
> errors only happen when you try to use the whole pipe (I think).
> 
> You would think that a bad cable would give you consistent errors at every 
> speed (since the same amount of electricity moves down the wire at the 
> same speed, regardless of data transfered).

Partly right, partly wrong.  The round-trip time for a cable is about
five nanoseconds per foot, so a 20 foot CAT5 with 100Mb/s data on it
(and half the edges making clocks) will have about 20 electrical 
transitions on it during a packet transfer.  All those transitions
can interfere with each other, and poorly made cables have a lot more
interference.  At 10Mb/s signalling rates, there are a lot fewer
transitions to interfere and the system is a lot more tolerant of
bad cables.

A network has some error correcting capability, but it takes time
to do this.  So a bad cable throwing a lot of physical-layer errors
may overrun the capability of the low-level drivers to deal with
them.  

Besides the cables, switches may have limited packet buffering
capability, so high packet rates may swamp them.  I can imagine
a cheap 100BT switch running out of processing power when hit with
the data rates that a Linux machine (as opposed to a windoze machine)
can produce.

If you are seeing packet errors, it might be worthwhile to log them
with tcpdump (to a big ramdisk) and see what their nature is.  But I
would not discount swapping cables and switches to see if they make
the problem go away.  My wife the doctor often learns which of five
diseases causes a set of symptoms by seeing which meds cure them.

Freegeek probably has a bin of cheap CAT5 cables, or Wacky Willies
might.  Inexpensive NEW cables can be found at www.pchcables.com of 
Hillsboro .

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

From jonlevitre at yahoo.com  Wed Mar 16 15:48:57 2005
From: jonlevitre at yahoo.com (Jon LeVitre)
Date: Wed, 16 Mar 2005 15:48:57 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] C programming question (distinguishing files vs
	directories/fifos/etc.)
Message-ID: <20050316234857.35632.qmail@web52705.mail.yahoo.com>

I'm writing a C program that reads from files.  What's the easiest way
to figure out whether a name is the name of a file (as opposed to a
directory, etc.)?

Under Linux, fopen() fails if you give it a directory name, but this
doesn't work under SunOS.

I noticed that open(name, O_RDWR) reports an error if you give it a
non-file.  It also reports an error if the user doesn't have write
permission.  Since I don't really need write permission, I can check
errno and call open again with O_RDONLY if it's a permission problem,
but this seems incredibly kludgy.

Jon
