From 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com  Wed Mar 16 16:06:26 2005
From: 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com (Steve Bonds)
Date: Wed, 16 Mar 2005 16:06:26 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] C programming question (distinguishing files vs
	directories/fifos/etc.)
In-Reply-To: <20050316234857.35632.qmail@web52705.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20050316234857.35632.qmail@web52705.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <22804-37690@sneakemail.com>

On Wed, 16 Mar 2005 15:48:57 -0800 (PST), Jon LeVitre  wrote:
> I'm writing a C program that reads from files.  What's the easiest way
> to figure out whether a name is the name of a file (as opposed to a
> directory, etc.)?

Use the stat() function on the name and use the POSIX macro S_ISDIR(m)
on the mode returned by stat().

  -- Steve


From jason at vancleve.com  Wed Mar 16 18:28:52 2005
From: jason at vancleve.com (Jason Van Cleve)
Date: Wed, 16 Mar 2005 18:28:52 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] I Want A Good Linux Software Diagramming Tool!
Message-ID: <20050316182852.37f619cf.jason@vancleve.com>

I think I'm going to lose it, here, fellows.  Visio is the one reason I
still rely on Windoesn't for developing software.  UML diagrams are
good, and I wouldn't want to design an application without them; but
there really isn't a Linux equivalent to Visio.  Argo, last I looked,
just doesn't hold a candle.

And yet, the Windon't machine I use for this purpose has been
spontaneously rebooting--a lot.  And the last couple of times this
happened, my Visio document was corrupted, so that Visio wouldn't open
it (even denied that it was a Visio file!).  So both times, my work was
lost permanently.  This is unacceptable.

I wanted to ask you all, once more, if there are ANY good UML tools for
Linux--anything better than Argo, just to raise a standard.  But now I'm
ready to bust my knuckles on this POS WinXP tower, and I would consider
almost any alternative, so long as it's Linux based.

Have you UML lovers any creative ideas, tools and techniques, that might
help me break my Visio addiction?  I've come to depend on UML diagrams
for design; and I'm almost ready to consider pencil and paper, but not
quite.  :]

--Jason V. C.

I'm out of my mind, but feel free to leave a message...

Jason,

   Have you looked at Poseidon or the UML plug-in to Eclipse? I started using
the former but I like the latter better. There's also EMF, the Eclipse
Modeling Framework, that lets you create your model in XML, with UML diagrams
or in code. It will then create the other forms for you.

   Eclipse, in its own way, is the GUI equivalent of emacs: it does
everything, including the dishes and waking you up in the morning.

Someone already mentioned Poseidon, which IIRC is written in Java. 
Technically it's non-free as a result. However, it does have something 
many other tools don't -- an interface to a performance modelling tool 
called PEPA, also written in Java. Do a web search for PEPA; it's from 
Edinburgh IIRC.

There is also Kivio. The basic tool is free, but I believe added 
templates cost money. I've never used Kivio. And ... there's Dia. Dia is 
Gnu free as in freedom, reasonable robust for something with a 0.9x 
version number, and has add-on software "dia2code" for generating code 
from UML. I've never used this part of it, so I can't testify to its 
usability.

Just in case you're interested in database modeling, Dia also has an 
add-on that does that, though I've forgotten what it's called. And there 
is DBDesigner4 -- another package written in Java. I've found that most 
large-scale Java-based packages run reliably only with the Sun JRE, so 
be careful.

Quoth Lance Means, on Wed, 16 Mar 2005 19:20:11 -0800:

> Have you checked out Inkscape? www.inkscape.org

FYI, from the FAQ:

"SVG is a useful format for creating diagrams, though, so we hope as
Inkscape grows as a fully-featured SVG editor, it will also be useful
for making attractive diagrams too. Several of us hope Inkscape will
become a useful technical drawing tool and work on features with that
goal in mind. However, Dia provides a number of useful capabilities such
as support for UML, autogeneration of diagrams, etc. that are well
beyond the scope of a general SVG editor."

to /etc/portage/package.keywords

to get them to emerge.

>For that matter, though, poseidon seems to offer the richest set of UML
>tools I've seen so far.  Nice interface, too.
>
>  
>
What little I've done with DBDesigner 4 was quite impressive. Being in 
Java, it will run on Windows, Linux and Solaris. It works well with 
MySQL, ODBC, Microsoft SQL Server and Postgresql IIRC.

From aaron at bavariati.org  Thu Mar 17 09:24:56 2005
From: aaron at bavariati.org (Aaron Burt)
Date: Thu, 17 Mar 2005 09:24:56 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] No scsi emulation
In-Reply-To: <1111079361.5880.8.camel@localhost.localdomain>
References: <1111079361.5880.8.camel@localhost.localdomain>
Message-ID: <20050317172456.GB9113@bavariati.org>

On Thu, Mar 17, 2005 at 09:09:21AM -0800, Dirk Ouellette wrote:
> I'm trying to burn an .iso from agnula.org but my FC3 didn't indtall the
> emulation. I've tried altering /boot/grub/grub.conf adding the hdc=ide-
> scsi hdd=ide-scsi ;

Are you loading the ide-scsi module after bootup?

Though really, IDE-SCSI is basically broken in 2.6.

You can simply tell CDRecord that the device is e.g. /dev/hdd and it
should work.  Remove the IDE-SCSI entries from Grub before you do
that, though.

Good luck,
  Aaron

Quoth M. Edward (Ed) Borasky, on Thu, 17 Mar 2005 05:51:44 -0800:

> >Hmm, I don't find an add-on for dia that provides a database modeling
> >stencil, as it were.  Database tools written for dia seem to require
> >an overloading of the UML class and association shapes, which really
> >aren't appropriate, IMO, for that type of modeling.
> >
> I think that's in "tedia2sql". By the way, "dbdesigner" and
> "tedia2sql" are masked in Gentoo. You need to add

tedia2sql will "Convert database ERD designed in Dia into SQL DDL
scripts."  So it's yet another dia-document-to-some-other-system
converter.  Apparently it works from "ER" diagrams, which is one set of
shapes that comes with dia.  This I don't understand, for there are only
five simple shapes under the "ER" option, none of which could begin to
describe a database table.  So it eludes me what sort of DDL might be
generated from such a simple form.

Again, it seems as though dia can only model database tables as UML
classes.

From jason at vancleve.com  Thu Mar 17 16:07:26 2005

Hi,

I could really use some help configuring my gentoo laptop to access our
printer at work.  Off-list would be fine.

No one at my workplace really understands network printing, and I don't
even know if we're using an actual print server.  The printer is an HP
4050N, and it's connected to the LAN (speaks TCP/IP).  So I have a model
number and an IP, and that's about all.

I tried the foomatic-configure script, but it barfed at line 1895 of
"DB.pm" for use of an uninitialized value.  Seems foomatic is still
buggy, and printing in Linux is still pretty much hit or miss.  I wish
someone in the know would describe cups, lpr, et al in terms of the
INTERFACES involved, the rules of the game, because everything I've read
is procedural and specific to different environments, and so it's
usually outdated or otherwise useless.

Anyway, I have cupsd running in Gentoo, and I think I need a "raw"
interface to the printer's IP address.  Any guidance on this doing this
without foomatic, please?

--Jason

From aaron at bavariati.org  Thu Mar 17 17:38:09 2005
From: aaron at bavariati.org (Aaron Burt)
Date: Thu, 17 Mar 2005 17:38:09 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] foomanual
In-Reply-To: <20050317160726.1d4793f3.jason@vancleve.com>
References: <20050317160726.1d4793f3.jason@vancleve.com>
Message-ID: <20050318013809.GF9113@bavariati.org>

On Thu, Mar 17, 2005 at 04:07:26PM -0800, Jason Van Cleve wrote:
> I tried the foomatic-configure script, but it barfed at line 1895 of
> "DB.pm" for use of an uninitialized value.  Seems foomatic is still
> buggy, and printing in Linux is still pretty much hit or miss.

Uhm, in Gentoo, at least.  CUPS and Foomatic have both been pretty
well-behaved for me for the past few years on various Deb and RPM
distros.  You might see if you can emerge a different version and see
if it works better.

> Anyway, I have cupsd running in Gentoo, and I think I need a "raw"
> interface to the printer's IP address.  Any guidance on this doing this
> without foomatic, please?

Actually, with HPs and other network printers, I've found that "raw"
(TCP socket, port 9100) mode tends to cause problems with jobs dying
halfway through or colliding with other jobs.  But every net print
device I've seen supports plain ol' LPR mode, printer=lp.  That works
nicely, with no job collisions or timeouts.

Sorry, can't remember how to set it up manually off the top of my
head, but if you have CUPS' web interface, you might try configuring
the printer via http://localhost:631 or just hand-edit
/etc/printers.conf (or whatever it's called.)

-- 
Your Favorite OS Sucks.

I have guessed out my solution.  The foomatic script having crapped out,
I tried connecting to the cups HTTP interface and got a login dialog,
which is not documented, AFAICT.  After trying several logins, I typed
in "root" and my system root password, and that did it.  Evidently, most
people open their Web browsers as root when doing this and do not
encounter the prompt.

So once I got into the configuration, I had to guess the DeviceURI,
since I had no idea what that was supposed to be.  I got lucky with
"socket://192.168.1.119:9100".  Where the hell is that URL documented,
please?  I can't even find a description of the different network
protocols that are used for printing, much less how to know which to use
for a particular printer.

After all, I'll say this:  printing with Linux is really easy--like so
many other things--provided you know exactly what you're doing! 
Personally, I've tackled it several times and remain, on the whole,
virtually clueless.

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Thu Mar 17 19:06:15 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Thu, 17 Mar 2005 19:06:15 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] foomanual
In-Reply-To: <20050318013809.GF9113@bavariati.org>
References: <20050317160726.1d4793f3.jason@vancleve.com>
	<20050318013809.GF9113@bavariati.org>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503171902520.14319@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Thu, 17 Mar 2005, Aaron Burt wrote:

> Actually, with HPs and other network printers, I've found that "raw" (TCP
> socket, port 9100) mode tends to cause problems with jobs dying halfway
> through or colliding with other jobs. But every net print device I've seen
> supports plain ol' LPR mode, printer=lp. That works nicely, with no job
> collisions or timeouts.

   I switched my HP LaserJet 5 and HP Professional Series 2500C from direct
connections to JetDirect cards. Made the changes in /etc/cups/printers.conf
and they've worked flawlessly ever since. Of course, it ain't a heavy load
here. Here's what I have specified:

# Printer configuration file for CUPS v1.1.21
# Written by cupsd on Wed Jan  5 11:11:51 2005
<DefaultPrinter colorp>
Info Color InkJet 2500C
Location office
DeviceURI socket://colorp:9100
State Idle
Accepting Yes
JobSheets none none
QuotaPeriod 0
PageLimit 0
KLimit 0
</Printer>
<Printer laser5>
Info LJ5 with no specifications
Location Office
DeviceURI socket://lj5:9100
State Idle
Accepting Yes
JobSheets none none
QuotaPeriod 0
PageLimit 0
KLimit 0
</Printer>
<Printer laser5_duplex>
Info Double-sided printing
Location office
DeviceURI socket://lj5:9100/
State Idle
Accepting Yes
JobSheets none none
QuotaPeriod 0
PageLimit 0
KLimit 0
</Printer>
<Printer laser5_single>
Info Single-sided printing
Location office
DeviceURI socket://lj5:9100
State Idle
Accepting Yes
JobSheets none none
QuotaPeriod 0
PageLimit 0
KLimit 0
</Printer>

HTH,

Rich

I was also going to suggest dia.  I have not used it for UML.
Just generalized block diagrams.  Earlier versions have crashed
on me, but I've never gotten a corrupted file.  And in any case,
the file is in XML, so you can edit it.  I've done that quite
a bit when I wanted to do a global edit that dia wanted me to
do the slow way.

I have a map of my house that I did with dia.  It shows all
the outlets and lights and indicates which breaker goes with
each.  I can tell it to hide that layer and instead show
the dimensions of the rooms.  There is quite a bit of info
in the file.  Chances are dia will do what you need.

Some distributions of Linux come with dia pre-installed.  Debian
has a .deb package.  I see there is a UML tutorial near the
top of this page.  http://www.gnome.org/projects/dia/links.html
That same page mentions that dia was inspired by visio, so you
may find the transition not too painful.

> Someone already mentioned Poseidon, which IIRC is written in Java. 
> Technically it's non-free as a result. However, it does have something 
> many other tools don't -- an interface to a performance modelling tool 
> called PEPA, also written in Java. Do a web search for PEPA; it's from 
> Edinburgh IIRC.
> 
> There is also Kivio. The basic tool is free, but I believe added 
> templates cost money. I've never used Kivio. And ... there's Dia. Dia is 
> Gnu free as in freedom, reasonable robust for something with a 0.9x 
> version number, and has add-on software "dia2code" for generating code 
> from UML. I've never used this part of it, so I can't testify to its 
> usability.
> 
> Just in case you're interested in database modeling, Dia also has an 
> add-on that does that, though I've forgotten what it's called. And there 
> is DBDesigner4 -- another package written in Java. I've found that most 
> large-scale Java-based packages run reliably only with the Sun JRE, so 
> be careful.

From hapibeli at comcast.net  Fri Mar 18 13:20:17 2005
From: hapibeli at comcast.net (Dirk Ouellette)
Date: Fri, 18 Mar 2005 13:20:17 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] cdrecord does not run with root privileges
Message-ID: <1111180817.19626.19.camel@localhost.localdomain>

How do I resolve this issue? K3b won't do it.
Thanks

cdrecord does not run with root privileges
It is highly recommended to configure cdrecord to run with root
privileges. Only then cdrecord runs with high priority which increases
the overall stability of the burning process. Apart from that it allows
changing the size of the used burning buffer. A lot of user problems
could be solved this way. This is also true when using SuSE's resmgr.
Solution: Use K3bSetup to solve this problem.
cdrdao does not run with root privileges
It is highly recommended to configure cdrdao to run with root privileges
to increase the overall stability of the burning process.
Solution: Use K3bSetup to solve this problem.

From shahms at shahms.com  Fri Mar 18 14:35:22 2005
From: shahms at shahms.com (Shahms King)
Date: Fri, 18 Mar 2005 14:35:22 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] cdrecord does not run with root privileges
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503181638240.6681@localhost>
References: <1111180817.19626.19.camel@localhost.localdomain>
	<Pine.LNX.4.61.0503181638240.6681@localhost>
Message-ID: <1111185322.11964.103.camel@shahms.mesd.k12.or.us>

My workaround was to:
1) install sudo
2) run visudo as root and add a line:

<username> ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD: /usr/bin/cdrecord, /usr/bin/cdrdao

3) put wrapper scripts in /usr/local/bin for cdrecord and cdrdao:

#!/sbin/sh
sudo /usr/bin/cdrecord "$@"

4) make sure they are executable
5) run "search" in k3b and tell it to use the programs in /usr/local/bin

Voila! it should work.

Also note that as long as k3b doesn't try and make cdrecord setuid root,
it (cdrecord) should run fine as an ordinary user if you have rw access
to the burner device, but will have a higher likelihood of buffer
underruns.

>>>>> "Roderick" == Roderick A Anderson <raanders at acm.org> writes:

Roderick> results.  Seems it might be more a DNS issue on their --
Roderick> USPS -- part.

Note that traceroute relies on ICMP packets being forwarded.  These
days, they are sometimes dropped at particular routers, which causes a
standard ping or traceroute to give confusing results.  More reliable
is something like tcptraceroute where the destination port is a real
open port.  E.g.:

  $ tcptraceroute www.usps.gov www
  Selected device eth0, address 192.168.0.3, port 50731 for outgoing packets
  Tracing the path to www.usps.gov (56.0.134.23) on TCP port 80 (www), 30 hops max

From griffint at pobox.com  Fri Mar 18 19:15:58 2005
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Fri, 18 Mar 2005 19:15:58 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] RPM/lib question
In-Reply-To: <20050319020241.GM9113@bavariati.org>
References: <20050319020241.GM9113@bavariati.org>
Message-ID: <200503181915.58485.griffint@pobox.com>

On Friday 18 March 2005 6:02 pm, Aaron Burt wrote:
> OK, weird one:  I'm building library RPMs from source tarballs, and
> in addition to .so files, I'm getting .a and .la files in /usr/lib. 
> What the heck are those, and should they go in the main binary
> package or in the -devel package?
>
> Anyone know?
>

The .a files should go in the -devel package. The .la files should go
in the library's main binary package.

The .a files are static libraries, used (optionally) only when building
applications.

The .la files are used by the libtool utility. They're basically an
abstraction layer on top of shared libraries intended to hide some
platform-specific dependencies.

Terry


From rich at paranoid.org  Fri Mar 18 21:16:26 2005
From: rich at paranoid.org (Rich Burroughs)
Date: Fri, 18 Mar 2005 21:16:26 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Route to USPS ( www.usps.gov )
In-Reply-To: <200503190218.j2J2ItHP087585@m5p.com>
References: <200503190218.j2J2ItHP087585@m5p.com>
Message-ID: <423BB5AA.7030900@paranoid.org>

Elliott Mitchell wrote:

> There is nothing you can do besides tell them it doesn't appear to be on
> your end (your e-mail makes it to this mailing list), and you cannot do
> any further diagnosis.

Well, there may be more that you can do than that :)

Are we talking about incoming mail to your server, outgoing, or both?

If it's outgoing, check your queue for the messages, and your mail log. 
Try to telnet to port 25 of their mail server and see what happens. You 
should be able to connect to their server and even type an email if you 
speak SMTP :) If you can't connect, then the error should give you a 
clue as to what's happening. If it's something like a spam blacklist 
involved, that may even show up in your maillog.

If it's incoming, mail only, then that's harder to troubleshoot on your 
end, their admin would need to check on their mail server.


Rich

> Note that traceroute relies on ICMP packets being forwarded.  These
> days, they are sometimes dropped at particular routers, which causes a
> standard ping or traceroute to give confusing results.  More reliable
> is something like tcptraceroute where the destination port is a real
> open port.  E.g.:
> 
>   $ tcptraceroute www.usps.gov www

- *.so   devel

On Friday 18 March 2005 9:30 pm, Paul Heinlein wrote:
> On Fri, 18 Mar 2005, Terry Griffin wrote:
> > The .a files should go in the -devel package. The .la files should
> > go in the library's main binary package.
>
> I don't even keep .la files any more. I delete them from the DESTDIR
> prior to packaging. In general,
>
> - *.so.* main package
> - *.so   devel
> - *.a    devel
>

Carefull on those *.so files. If there are no *.so.* files then the
*.so files need to go in the main package, or if the *.so.* files are
symbolic links to the *.so files, then again the *.so files need to
go in to the main package.

Or to simplify: Put the *.so files in the main package _unless_ there
are specific provisions that make that unnecessary. One such provision
is non-symlink *.so.* files.

Terry


From ehem at m5p.com  Sat Mar 19 13:02:31 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Sat, 19 Mar 2005 13:02:31 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] RPM/lib question
In-Reply-To: <20050319200016.101774248@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200503192102.j2JL2VWH009685@m5p.com>

>From: Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>
> I don't even keep .la files any more. I delete them from the DESTDIR 
> prior to packaging. In general,
> 
> - *.so.* main package
> - *.so   devel
> - *.a    devel

The .la files should definitely be in devel. If you ever develop or
build GTK/Glib programs you'll need them. Debian generally places the *.a
files into -dbg (debug) packages.


>From: Terry Griffin <griffint at pobox.com>
> Carefull on those *.so files. If there are no *.so.* files then the
> *.so files need to go in the main package, or if the *.so.* files are
> symbolic links to the *.so files, then again the *.so files need to
> go in to the main package.

The *.so.* files should NEVER be links to the *.so files. Conventional
setup is <lib>.so -> <lib>.so.<major> -> <lib>.so.<fullversion>, where
<lib>.so.<fullversion> is the actual library.

> Or to simplify: Put the *.so files in the main package _unless_ there
> are specific provisions that make that unnecessary. One such provision
> is non-symlink *.so.* files.

This is not a provision, this is STANDARD practice! I haven't fully
explored the issue, but I believe using gcc as a front end to ld will
always unwind one level of symbolic links. I'm unsure whether it checks
for a filename of the form *.so.[0-9], but if you look at what ldd tells
you output always links to <lib>.so.[0-9].

From heinlein at madboa.com  Sat Mar 19 13:59:10 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Sat, 19 Mar 2005 13:59:10 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] RPM/lib question
In-Reply-To: <200503192102.j2JL2VWH009685@m5p.com>

Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0503191355430.24871@pecos.madboa.com>

On Sat, 19 Mar 2005, Elliott Mitchell wrote:

> The *.so.* files should NEVER be links to the *.so files. 
> Conventional setup is <lib>.so -> <lib>.so.<major> -> 
> <lib>.so.<fullversion>, where <lib>.so.<fullversion> is the actual 
> library.
>
>> Or to simplify: Put the *.so files in the main package _unless_ 
>> there are specific provisions that make that unnecessary. One such 
>> provision is non-symlink *.so.* files.
>
> This is not a provision, this is STANDARD practice! I haven't fully 
> explored the issue, but I believe using gcc as a front end to ld 
> will always unwind one level of symbolic links. I'm unsure whether 
> it checks for a filename of the form *.so.[0-9], but if you look at 
> what ldd tells you output always links to <lib>.so.[0-9].

Binaries compiled with gcc and GNU ld never look for libfoo.so; they 
always look for libfoo.so.X. That's why the *.so files can be packaged 
with the -devel stuff. If you need the *.so symlinks, it's only at 
compile time, never at run time.

-- Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>


From griffint at pobox.com  Sat Mar 19 15:19:26 2005
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Sat, 19 Mar 2005 15:19:26 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] RPM/lib question
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0503191355430.24871@pecos.madboa.com>
References: <200503192102.j2JL2VWH009685@m5p.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.62.0503191355430.24871@pecos.madboa.com>
Message-ID: <200503191519.26154.griffint@pobox.com>

On Saturday 19 March 2005 1:59 pm, Paul Heinlein wrote:
> On Sat, 19 Mar 2005, Elliott Mitchell wrote:
> > The *.so.* files should NEVER be links to the *.so files.
> > Conventional setup is <lib>.so -> <lib>.so.<major> ->
> > <lib>.so.<fullversion>, where <lib>.so.<fullversion> is the actual
> > library.
> >
> >> Or to simplify: Put the *.so files in the main package _unless_
> >> there are specific provisions that make that unnecessary. One such
> >> provision is non-symlink *.so.* files.
> >
> > This is not a provision, this is STANDARD practice! I haven't fully
> > explored the issue, but I believe using gcc as a front end to ld
> > will always unwind one level of symbolic links. I'm unsure whether
> > it checks for a filename of the form *.so.[0-9], but if you look at
> > what ldd tells you output always links to <lib>.so.[0-9].
>
> Binaries compiled with gcc and GNU ld never look for libfoo.so; they
> always look for libfoo.so.X. That's why the *.so files can be packaged
> with the -devel stuff. If you need the *.so symlinks, it's only at
> compile time, never at run time.
>
> -- Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

I don't know where you get that. If you say:

   gcc somefile.c -lsomelib

then ld is going to look for libsomelib.so. If it finds it then
that's the reference that will go in the binary even if libsomelib.so
is a symbolic link to libsomelib.so.X (which it often is). With -l it
will never look for libsomelib.so.X. If it can't find libsomelib.so
then it goes on to look for libsomelib.a.

If you really want the reference to libsomelib.so.X to end up in
the application's binary then you can't use the -l switch. You have
to say something like:

   gcc somefile.c /path/to/libsomelib.so.X

which I've no doubt is very common in make files or the ./configure
scripts that generate make files. But it's not something gcc or ld
do automatically.

Terry

> that's the reference that will go in the binary even if libsomelib.so
> is a symbolic link to libsomelib.so.X (which it often is).

Without trying to sound like I know what's *supposed* to happen, 
that's not the way it works on my box (CentOS 4.0, gcc 3.4.3, glibc 
2.3.4). If I do a general -lz, it appears to me that the linker 
unravels the symlinks. Or is this a bad test?

[tmp]$ cat t.c
#include <stdio.h>
int main() { printf( "Hello, world!\n" ); return 0; }

[tmp]$ ls -og /usr/lib/libz.so
lrwxrwxrwx  1 15 Mar 18 13:54 /usr/lib/libz.so -> libz.so.1.2.1.2*

[tmp]$ gcc -o t -lz t.c

[tmp]$ file t
t: ELF 32-bit LSB executable, Intel 80386, version 1 (SYSV), for 
GNU/Linux 2.2.5, dynamically linked (uses shared libs), not stripped

[tmp]$ ldd t
         libz.so.1 => /usr/lib/libz.so.1 (0x00850000)
         libc.so.6 => /lib/tls/libc.so.6 (0x00631000)
         /lib/ld-linux.so.2 (0x00618000)

[tmp]$ strings t | grep libz
libz.so.1

-- Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

problem?

Question Two:  Why the need for multiple reboots and fscks across the root
file system?

Curious. I get that with libz also (FC3). But if I build my own .so
library then gcc behaves in the way I described. In fact I can mix
libz and my shared library in a single app and get the two different
types of references in the app's binary.

The possibility that it's following the symlinks doesn't make sense.
My libz symlinks are:

  /usr/lib/libz.so -> libz.so.1.2.1.2
  /usr/lib/libz.so.1 -> libz.so.1.2.1.2

The -lz switch would take you to libz.so. From there gcc could
easily hop to libz.so.1.2.1.2, but getting from there back to
libz.so.1 would be very weird and very inefficient. But somehow
that's what ends up in the app binary.

There's some magic going on under the hood I think.

Terry

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Sat Mar 19 22:09:47 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sat, 19 Mar 2005 22:09:47 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] FSCK what's going on?
In-Reply-To: <200503200532.j2K5WTX23554@pop.hevanet.com>
References: <200503200532.j2K5WTX23554@pop.hevanet.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503192202340.3891@localhost>

What do you mean when you say "ran a fsck from knoppix"?  Did you run an
"e2fsck" without the -f option, or did you run an actual "fsck"?  You
say the checked out clean.  Was this right away when running the fsck
command, or after a lengthy disk check?  e2fsck without a -f will often
not even bother to run a disk check.

I like to run "e2fsck -fptv" (sometimes with the -c option to run
badblocks).  If that doesn't succeed, I then run "fsck -C".  That has
always worked for me.  I also use knoppix for this procedure.

e2fsck is a wrapper around fsck.ext3.  I'm thinking it's kinda pointless to
run e2fsck.  Maybe use fsck directly instead.

   will attempt to load the shared object specified by the DT_SONAME
   field rather than the using the file name given to the linker.

the VirtualHost section of the httpd.conf file at the end of this eamil.

I have a set of files in var/www/html which serve OK when I enter 
209.210.229.130 in a web browser. This is as it was before I tried to add 
virtual hosting. A second web site located at /var/www/wschopp/html behaves 
as follows:

Enter www.schoppformetro.com into a browser and you get the Fedora Core 
Test Page (I presume that this means it works)

Enter http://www.schoppformetro.com/index.html into a browser and you get :
Forbidden, You don't have permission to access /index.html on this 
server,Additionally, a 403 Forbidden error was encountered while trying to 
use an ErrorDocument to handle the request. (I take that this is a 
permissions problem, but I think the permissions are set the same as for 
the files that work from var/www/html. All of these files were created on 
Windows and moved to the Linux box with a pen drive.)

Before I started mucking around with the config file, entering 
www.schoppformetro.com into a browser would get the index.htm from 
/var/www/html. Of course I want to serve up files from wschopp/html 
wherever it must be put.

(mclp.org does not point to this IP address yet)

Once this problem is solved, I hope to add 3-5 more virtual hosts.

Any suggestions?

Thanks
JK

---------------------------------------------
<VirtualHost *:80>
	ServerName 209.210.229.130
	DocumentRoot /var/www/html
   	ServerSignature email
  	DirectoryIndex  index.php index.html index.htm index.shtml
  	LogLevel  warn
  	HostNameLookups off
</VirtualHost>

# Virtual host Virtual Host 0
<VirtualHost *:80>
	ServerName www.schoppformetro.com
  	ServerAlias schoppformetro.com
	DocumentRoot /var/www/wschopp/html
	DirectoryIndex  index.php index.html index.htm index.shtml
</VirtualHost>

# Virtual host Virtual Host 1
<VirtualHost *:80>
	ServerName www.mclp.org
  	ServerAlias mclp.org
  	DocumentRoot /var/wmclp/html/
</VirtualHost>

From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Sun, 20 Mar 2005 09:06:25 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] RPM/lib question - solved
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.62.0503192208570.24871@pecos.madboa.com>
References: <200503192102.j2JL2VWH009685@m5p.com>
	<200503192137.20294.griffint@pobox.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.62.0503192208570.24871@pecos.madboa.com>
Message-ID: <200503200906.25900.griffint@pobox.com>

On Saturday 19 March 2005 10:15 pm, Paul Heinlein wrote:
> On Sat, 19 Mar 2005, Terry Griffin wrote:
> > On Saturday 19 March 2005 5:24 pm, Paul Heinlein wrote:
> >> On Sat, 19 Mar 2005, Terry Griffin wrote:

> >>

> >> linker unravels the symlinks. Or is this a bad test?
> >

> >

> > sense. My libz symlinks are:

> >

> > that's what ends up in the app binary.
> >
> > There's some magic going on under the hood I think.
>
> What do you bet it's the "-soname" option passed to the linker when
> building the library? From the ld(1) man page:
>
>    When an executable is linked with a shared object which has a
>    DT_SONAME field, then when the executable is run the dynamic
> linker will attempt to load the shared object specified by the
> DT_SONAME field rather than the using the file name given to the
> linker.
>
> -- Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

Bingo. If I build my shared library with the -soname option and then
link my app to that library, the name given by -soname is what ends
up in the app's binary, not the actual name of the library file.

Now back to the original RPM question, the answer is the infamous
"it depends."

1) If the library is built without the -soname option, then the .so
file must go in to the library's main binary package, not the -devel
package.

2) If it is built using -soname, then a file or symlink matching the
name given by -soname must go in the main binary package. The
original .so file may go in to the -devel package instead of the main
package.

3) If you're not sure how the library was built then follow #1.

Terry


From griffint at pobox.com  Sun Mar 20 09:34:04 2005
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Sun, 20 Mar 2005 09:34:04 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] RPM/lib question - solved
In-Reply-To: <200503200906.25900.griffint@pobox.com>
References: <200503192102.j2JL2VWH009685@m5p.com>
	<Pine.LNX.4.62.0503192208570.24871@pecos.madboa.com>
	<200503200906.25900.griffint@pobox.com>
Message-ID: <200503200934.04927.griffint@pobox.com>

On Sunday 20 March 2005 9:06 am, Terry Griffin wrote:
> On Saturday 19 March 2005 10:15 pm, Paul Heinlein wrote:
> > On Sat, 19 Mar 2005, Terry Griffin wrote:
> > > On Saturday 19 March 2005 5:24 pm, Paul Heinlein wrote:
> > >> On Sat, 19 Mar 2005, Terry Griffin wrote:
> > >>> I don't know where you get that. If you say:
> > >>>
> > >>>   gcc somefile.c -lsomelib
> > >>>
> > >>> then ld is going to look for libsomelib.so. If it finds it then
> > >>> that's the reference that will go in the binary even if
> > >>> libsomelib.so is a symbolic link to libsomelib.so.X (which it
> > >>> often is).
> > >>
> > >> Without trying to sound like I know what's *supposed* to happen,
> > >> that's not the way it works on my box (CentOS 4.0, gcc 3.4.3,
> > >> glibc 2.3.4). If I do a general -lz, it appears to me that the
> > >> linker unravels the symlinks. Or is this a bad test?
> > >
> > > Curious. I get that with libz also (FC3). But if I build my own
> > > .so library then gcc behaves in the way I described. In fact I
> > > can mix libz and my shared library in a single app and get the
> > > two different types of references in the app's binary.
> > >
> > > The possibility that it's following the symlinks doesn't make
> > > sense. My libz symlinks are:
> > >
> > >  /usr/lib/libz.so -> libz.so.1.2.1.2
> > >  /usr/lib/libz.so.1 -> libz.so.1.2.1.2
> > >
> > > The -lz switch would take you to libz.so. From there gcc could
> > > easily hop to libz.so.1.2.1.2, but getting from there back to
> > > libz.so.1 would be very weird and very inefficient. But somehow
> > > that's what ends up in the app binary.
> > >
> > > There's some magic going on under the hood I think.
> >
> > What do you bet it's the "-soname" option passed to the linker when
> > building the library? From the ld(1) man page:
> >
> >    When an executable is linked with a shared object which has a
> >    DT_SONAME field, then when the executable is run the dynamic
> > linker will attempt to load the shared object specified by the
> > DT_SONAME field rather than the using the file name given to the
> > linker.
> >
> > -- Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>
>
> Bingo. If I build my shared library with the -soname option and then
> link my app to that library, the name given by -soname is what ends
> up in the app's binary, not the actual name of the library file.
>
> Now back to the original RPM question, the answer is the infamous
> "it depends."
>
> 1) If the library is built without the -soname option, then the .so
> file must go in to the library's main binary package, not the -devel
> package.
>
> 2) If it is built using -soname, then a file or symlink matching the
> name given by -soname must go in the main binary package. The
> original .so file may go in to the -devel package instead of the main
> package.
>
> 3) If you're not sure how the library was built then follow #1.
>
> Terry

Following up on myself...

I figured there had to be a easy way to determine if -soname was
used to build the library, and there is.

   objdump -p /path/to/binary-lib-file.so | grep SONAME

You'll get nothing if -soname was not used or the SONAME value
if -soname was used. With this you can figure out what needs to
go in the main RPM and what can go in the -devel RPM instead.

Terry


From ehem at m5p.com  Sun Mar 20 13:42:43 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Sun, 20 Mar 2005 13:42:43 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] RPM/lib question - solved
In-Reply-To: <20050320170652.151524269@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200503202142.j2KLgh3P024920@m5p.com>

>From: Terry Griffin <griffint at pobox.com>
> Now back to the original RPM question, the answer is the infamous
> "it depends."
> 
> 1) If the library is built without the -soname option, then the .so
> file must go in to the library's main binary package, not the -devel
> package.
> 
> 2) If it is built using -soname, then a file or symlink matching the
> name given by -soname must go in the main binary package. The
> original .so file may go in to the -devel package instead of the main
> package.
> 
> 3) If you're not sure how the library was built then follow #1.

True, but the number of libraries that don't set SONAME could likely be
counted by a stupid person who was missing one arm and without taking off
either sock. You've got a 99% chance it is set with any random library
you run across. I strongly suspect Debian's packaging guidelines may well
require this (at least ones from them consistantly confine the .so link
to -dev packages).

Another simple test would be to simply do a "Hello, world" program and
link it to the library and see what `ldd` prints out.

From ehem at m5p.com  Sun Mar 20 13:49:44 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Sun, 20 Mar 2005 13:49:44 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] FSCK what's going on?
In-Reply-To: <20050320170652.151524269@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200503202149.j2KLniet024985@m5p.com>

>From: Carlos Konstanski <ckonstan at lunarlogic.com>
> What do you mean when you say "ran a fsck from knoppix"?  Did you run an
> "e2fsck" without the -f option, or did you run an actual "fsck"?  You
> say the checked out clean.  Was this right away when running the fsck
> command, or after a lengthy disk check?  e2fsck without a -f will often
> not even bother to run a disk check.

(Because it checks the clean flag on the filesystem, and unless there is
a panic or other unclean shutdown that does tend to get reset.)

> e2fsck is a wrapper around fsck.ext3.  I'm thinking it's kinda pointless to
> run e2fsck.  Maybe use fsck directly instead.

Other way around. `fsck` is a pretty simple wrapper for `fsck.<fs>`
(where <fs> is "ext2", "ext3" or whatever). `fsck.ext2` and `fsck.ext3`
are generally symbolic links to `e2fsck`. The fun part is unless the FS
is actively marked as dirty (kernel checks found inconsistancies) or it
has exceeded the mount count, `fsck.ext3` is a no-op as it lets the
kernel do journal playback.

Rich,

perl -MCPAN -e shell

gives you the install shell

cpan>install Tk

Then will go out and get the Tk module.

afterwards you can either install another module or 

cpan>quit

Currently the install is still going.  It's either quit or exit.

> Be careful installing sixpack with perl?  Living in the Northwest you will

> as if you install just 'sixpack' you are likely to get just Budweiser and

Josh,

   Groan! But, I guess that I asked for this reaction.

   Some of you -- particularly students and others who write in LaTeX/LyX
might appreciate this bibliographic reference manager. It maintains a bibtex
database (searchable), will download from on-line reference databases, and
will integrate with LyX/LaTeX. Has both cli and gui modes.

   I tried getting a java tool working but failed (the system couldn't find
java on my box -- and it's there). Really wanted to use pybibliographer but
that's a gnome application that wants much more than the core libraries. I
got tired of chasing gnome dependencies and gave up.

   The best way of getting sixpack is from sourceforge (also get bp so you can
translate different reference database formats). I grabbed the rpms, ran them
through rpm2tgz, then used Slackware's installpkg to install them. Worked
like a charm.

Rich

From alan at clueserver.org  Wed Mar 23 15:40:53 2005
From: alan at clueserver.org (Alan)

On Wed, 2005-03-23 at 06:57 -0800, Michael Montagne wrote:
> I was doing a netstat -n on my server at work this morning and noticed
> these two connections.  Seem awfully odd to me.  Should I be worried?
> How can investigate further?
> 
> tcp        0      0 10.10.10.100:55519      66.197.0.145:6667 ESTABLISHED
> tcp        0      0 10.10.10.100:36921      193.110.95.1:6667 ESTABLISHED 

Be afraid. Be very afraid.

If you or one of your users using IRC, you may have been hacked.

The last few hacked systems I have seen had IRC reflectors installed on
them.

chkrootkit and other rootkit detectors are your friend.  Using netcat to
observe the traffic is also helpful.

Here is what the addresses translate to:

[alan at dagon ~]$ host 193.110.95.1
1.95.110.193.in-addr.arpa domain name pointer
carouge.ch.eu.undernet.org.
[alan at dagon ~]$ host 66.197.0.145
145.0.197.66.in-addr.arpa domain name pointer rhodium.4ph.com.

Looks like a reflector to me.

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Wed Mar 23 15:44:36 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Wed, 23 Mar 2005 15:44:36 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] video help please, and I swear I won'
In-Reply-To: <032320052246.7888.4241F1C30009429B00001ED022007358340B030B9C079D9D0E08D2040A0E080C0703@comcast.net>
References: <032320052246.7888.4241F1C30009429B00001ED022007358340B030B9C079D9D0E08D2040A0E080C0703@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503231533150.4818@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Wed, 23 Mar 2005, Michael D. Harris D.M.D. wrote:

> I would like to know how to go undo this portion of that wizard, or what
> file I have to edit. I have tried and plan on trying xf86config when I get
> home tonight.

Mike,

   The file you want is /etc/X11/xf86config (or /etc/X11/xorg.conf). Go look
in the Monitor section. Both of my desktop systems run xorg-6.8.1 and in
/etc/X11/xorg.conf I have:

# Monitor section
Section "Monitor"

     Identifier  "Hyundai LCD"
     HorizSync   31-80
     VertRefresh 56-75

EndSection

  Then there's:

Section "Device"
     Identifier "ATI Rage 128 Pro Ultra"
     Driver     "r128"
EndSection

   My other desktop has an nVidia:

Section "Device"
     Identifier  "nVidia GeForce2 MX/400"
     Driver      "nv"
     #VideoRam    32768
EndSection

   This works for me.

HTH,

Rich

From ehem at m5p.com  Wed Mar 23 19:21:00 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Wed, 23 Mar 2005 19:21:00 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Mysterious connections
In-Reply-To: <20050324025018.55AFF426C@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200503240321.j2O3L08g074086@m5p.com>

>From: Michael Montagne <michael at themontagnes.com>
> So, if that is the case and I block all IRC traffic at the firewall
> and chkrootkit and rkhunter both come out negative.  Perhaps I've
> averted disaster. I don't need IRC and probably never will. 
> Of course a password sniffer or keystroke logger could've been
> installed.  But I hardly ever work on that box except thru an ssh
> session from a different machine, doea that insulate me from those
> nasty tools?

If those two IRC sessions cannot be directly attributed to one of your
users, I'd still be really worried. Perhaps they used a more recent
rootkit, that those do not yet detect.

Blocking IRC is irrelevant, that just blocks the standard control method,
it doesn't keep them out. There are other methods to control a zombie,
and they're already in your machine.

Adjusting ssh/sshd to sniff passwords isn't a big deal for an intruder.
Just another program that needs to be backdoored. Only hitting one tool
might be easier, but figure these are robots doing the work and once they
can do one the cost is minimal for them. I already know of an incident
where the ssh client was made to log passwords.

It's the file that X (version 4 and later) uses, and that's what counts.  
When you run startx, startkde, or '/etc/init.d/?dm 
start', /etc/X11/XF86Config-4 is the default config file.

  man XF86Config

# The following was supposedly scribed by
# Eric Wilhelm
# on Thursday 24 March 2005 02:08 pm:

>>I noticed I have a file xf86config and one called xf86config-4. ?The
>> -4 file has info in it concerning and nVidia card and this file does
>> not get altered when I run xf86config.

>Sounds like something is wrong with your xf86config setup.

Nevermind that.  Looks like there is no setup (maybe the filename is 
compiled in?)  The "something wrong" is with the xf86config program 
(and it's lack of configurability.)

I just use a text editor (but make a backup copy before you start.)  
Look at the man pages, etc.  Most of the configuration sections have a 
man page under "4x".

  man -S 4x mouse

Not sure how to get "apropos" to help you out here, but you can at least 
find where some of the X manpages are (could be all of them) by asking 
man where it found the mouse page:

  man -S 4x -w mouse

xf86cfg is sometimes helpful (though it might not put the config file in 
the right place either.)

From griffint at pobox.com  Thu Mar 24 12:21:14 2005

On Thursday 24 March 2005 11:48 am, Michael D. Harris D.M.D. wrote:
> I noticed I have a file xf86config and one called xf86config-4.  The
> -4 file has info in it concerning and nVidia card and this file does
> not get altered when I run xf86config.  Could that file be the one my
> system used prior to my doing the upgrade, and if so, how do I get it
> to be used again?
>

What distro and version are you running? What were you running before
the upgrade?

There was a transition period between XFree86 3.x and 4.x where distros
would ship with both versions because not all drivers had been ported
from 3.x to 4.x. So depending on what video card you had it would use
either 3.x or 4.x and get the config info from file xf86config or
xf86config-4 respectively.

Terry

From ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net  Thu Mar 24 15:29:58 2005
From: ewilhelm at sbcglobal.net (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Thu, 24 Mar 2005 17:29:58 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] man sections
In-Reply-To: <20050324142314.4e8724c7.jason@vancleve.com>
References: <032420051948.10222.42431976000787AB000027EE22069997350B030B9C079D9D0E08D2040A0E080C0703@comcast.net>
	<200503241424.45473.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>
	<20050324142314.4e8724c7.jason@vancleve.com>
Message-ID: <200503241729.58570.ewilhelm@sbcglobal.net>

# The following was supposedly scribed by
# Jason Van Cleve
# on Thursday 24 March 2005 04:23 pm:

Assuming this was intended for the list...

>> man page under "4x".
>>
>> ? man -S 4x mouse
>
>What's that -S option do, pray tell? ?I'm reading "colon separated
>section list" in the help, but what's "4x"?

That's a section name.

  ls /usr/share/man/

  ls /usr/X11R6/man/

(Finding the corresponding directory on a not-sarge system is left as an 
exercise for the reader.)  Notice that things are split into 
directories.  I don't think that really matters.  Rather I think man 
refers to the .4x in the filenames like "mouse.4x.gz".  So, when you 
say 'whatis mouse' or 'apropos mouse' and see (4) or (3ncurses) or 
(4x), those are the section numbers.  In the case of 'whatis mouse', 
you get:

  mouse (4)            - serial mouse interface
  mouse (3ncurses)     - mouse interface through curses
  mouse (4x)           - Mouse input driver
  
Which means that 'man mouse' is just going to give you the first and 
with 'man -a mouse' you would have to cycle through them one at a time, 
so use "-S 4x" to say "Show me the manpage for 'mouse' from section 
4x."

I guess the other directories are for locales.  If you're really 
interested, read more of 'man man'.

  man -L ko -S 5 passwd

I happen to really like the man system.  Not sure why gnu "shuns it so" 
in favor of info (I guess that's the cathedral talking.)  Really wish 
kde had man pages.

I learned most of what I know from man and apropos.  If you can't find 
it there, you either need to find the howto or what you want to do 
hasn't been done before.  Maybe it's not the easiest way to learn a 
system, but you're less likely to be deceived or underinformed (and 
your understanding of what's really going on will be better) if you get 
your knowledge straight from the source (I learned most of what I know 
about Perl from perldoc, and that keeps me from falling into a lot of 
common traps.)  Okay.  Time to load this soapbox onto the truck so...

  http://www.osnews.com/story.php?news_id=6282

--Eric

OK, I got everything working, but as usual with printing, I understand
nooooooooooothing.

For comparison with my original cupsd.conf, here is the one that works:

LogFilePerm 0600
MaxLogSize 2000000000
LogLevel info
Printcap /etc/printcap
<Location />
Order Deny,Allow
Deny From All
Allow From All
</Location>
<Location /admin>
AuthType Basic
AuthClass System
Order Deny,Allow
Deny From All
Allow From 127.0.0.1
</Location>
<Location /printers/hp1200>
Order Deny,Allow
Deny From All
Allow From 127.0.0.1
AuthType None
Allow from All
</Location>
<Location /printers/epsoncolor>
Order Deny,Allow
Deny From All
Allow From 127.0.0.1
AuthType None
Allow from All
</Location>
Browsing On
BrowseProtocols cups
BrowseOrder Deny,Allow
BrowseAllow from @LOCAL
BrowseAddress 255.255.255.255
Listen *:631

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Thu Mar 24 17:57:34 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Thu, 24 Mar 2005 17:57:34 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Fixed a spurious interrupt problem
Message-ID: <20050325015734.GA7431@gate.kl-ic.com>


I use an old IBM Thinkpad 560 running Fedora Core 1 as a firewall.
Small, low power, etc.  However, I have had a long term problem that
I finally got around to fixing today, after a very laborious network
upgrade from RH8 to FC1 (which is another story).  This is an older
laptop, with a 133MHz processor, 72MB RAM, and almost nothing built
in;  the inner and outer ethernet ports are both PCMCIA cards,  3Com
3CCFEM556B 10/100 LAN + 56K, using the 3c574 driver for the ethernet
portion of the card.

The problem was frequent (about 6/minute) messages in dmesg and in
/var/log/messages:

kernel: eth1: interrupt(s) dropped!

I only got these messages for eth1, not eth0 .

Linux put the eth0 card at irq 3 and the eth1 card at irq 5.  In
theory, irq 5 belongs to a second parallel port, but there is not
one in the laptop.  However, I was a little worried by potential
interactions with parallel port code in the kernel, so I turned 
off irq 5 with these lines added to  /etc/pcmcia/config.opts :

exclude irq 5 
exclude irq 9

I added the second line because irq 9 is sometimes treated as a
shared interrupt (IIRC) - I wanted to force usage of irq 10.

The card is now on irq 10, and I no longer see the annoying error
messages.  I don't know whether this will improve performance
(it should), but at least the log files are smaller.

Perhaps this will help somebody else, so I am sharing it here.  If
it helps you, return the favor by posting a fix that you discovered!

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

because they would not have renamed the configuration file without a
good reason.  Wouldn't they?!?  The current version of XFree86 uses the
xorg.conf file name for the configuration.

On Thu, 24 Mar 2005, Kenneth G. Stephens wrote:

> Early version of XFree86 used the XF86Config-4 file.  I linked the
> XF86Config-4 to the XF86Config file. Probably the wrong thing to do because
> they would not have renamed the configuration file without a good reason.
> Wouldn't they?!? The current version of XFree86 uses the xorg.conf file
> name for the configuration.

   If I'm not mistaken, Ken, the earlier versions of XFree86 (3.x and lower)
used XF86Config and the latest versions use the XF96Config-4 file. However,
there are licensing issues with XFree86 that cropped up a year or so ago.
X.org forked from XFree86 and provides an equivalent -- but completely
unencumbered -- X Window System for linux and other F/OSS. The X.org config
file is /etc/X11/xorg.conf. See <http://www.x.org/>. Their first release was
x.org-6.7; they've just released x.org-6.8.2.

Rich

On Thu, 24 Mar 2005, Michael Harris wrote:

> Ok, so, what I really want is for my X to start.  Are there some other
> tools I can use to help? I have tried editing the XF86Config file to
> resemble the XF86Config-4 file in the monitor and device sections that
> concern video and have had no luck. I am bound and determined to make it
> work via editing in one way or another, but I am getting frustrated,
> because it worked so well before I did that apt-get upgrade thing,

Mike,

   Aha! Now we're getting to the heart of the problem: X won't start, eh? I
had this problem not too long ago and it turned out to be a case mismatch
between what Xfce expected and what it found in xorg.conf.

   In my case the config file, by default, has a section named "Keyboard".
Xfce was looking for a section named "keyboard". I found the problem by
looking at /var/log/Xorg.0.log where I saw that "keyboard" could not be
found. Your installation will have a similar file for your X server and
desktop/window manager. Look in there for insight.

HTH,

Rich

Applied Ecosystem Services, Inc. (TM)
<http://www.appl-ecosys.com>   Voice: 503-667-4517   Fax: 503-667-8863


From raanders at acm.org  Fri Mar 25 07:24:31 2005
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Fri, 25 Mar 2005 07:24:31 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Solved:  Route to USPS.GOV
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0503250718370.21719-100000@main.cyber-office.net>

Well this is kind of embarassing but the issue was name servers.  The part 
that makes me feel better is several ISPs in the area , including a rather 
large one , got caught by it also.

It came down to using the inclusive internet DNS root servers ( OpenNIC
<http://www.opennic.unrated.net/>) which either went completely off line
or were renumbered.  I somehow missed ( or got dropped off the announce
mailing list ) the change.

A few quick digs and a rebuild of the '@' file ( dnscache ) and all was 
well again.  Thanks to everyone that replied to my plea for help.

Subject: [PLUG] Tk Configuration
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503231711270.4818@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0503250725020.21719-100000@main.cyber-office.net>

On Wed, 23 Mar 2005, Rich Shepard wrote:

>    Anyone here know how to make a Tk interface display in a larger font? I
> know of qtconfig, and I can change the display font in gtk+, but this is new
> to me. I'd like to increase the size of the text in the menus as well as in
> the document displayed.

Sorry to take so long.  I did forget to look for the book when I got home.  
( In my defense I came home to a wife with the flu. ) 

A quick look in "Learning Perl/Tk" gave this ( untested ) code.

$widget->fontConfigure(fontname, -size=> 24);

Where 'fontname' can be anything you might have created ( but probably did
not ) or the system determined replacements for 'courier' , 'times' , or
'helvetica'.  A positive 'size' yields a font sized in points and a
negative in pixels.


HTH,

Let's see.

After a bit of time fiddling and lunch I decided for my interpretation of 
your stated want/need that you should use the -font attribute in the menu 
creation/definition. 

my $mw = MainWindow->new;
$mw->title( "Yada Yada" );
...
$menu1 = $mw->Menu( ... -font => ['courier', 24] ... )->pack( );
#                       ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^
...

From heinlein at madboa.com  Fri Mar 25 15:05:22 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Fri, 25 Mar 2005 15:05:22 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Sendmail config question
In-Reply-To: <9e0a3578050325135772f61b3@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9e0a35780503251246711af6df@mail.gmail.com>
	<Pine.OSX.4.62.0503251341530.864@arrowhead.galois.com>
	<9e0a3578050325135772f61b3@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.62.0503251455150.864@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Fri, 25 Mar 2005, Matt Alexander wrote:

> Sorry, that was a little confusing.  I'd like email to appear as
> user at mydomain.com, not as user at host.mydomain.com.
>
> Here's the problem, I have scripts running from cron that page my
> cellphone.  The sending servers do not have external DNS entries.  My
> cell company then bounces these with this message:
>
> 553 host.mydomain.com does not exist
>
> So, I'm hoping that I can configure Sendmail on each box to make the
> outgoing SMTP conversation using only mydomain.com.

Try setting the masquerade_envelope feature in your sendmail.mc file:

FEATURE(`masquerade_envelope')

Also, make sure there aren't any "exposed" users, usernames that 
always use the internal site name rather than the masqueraded name.

--Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

> Mike
lspci gives you your video card.
www.xfree86.org check the hardware list for which driver to use.
Get your monitor information.  Vertical and Horizontal Frequencies.  
Use your current Xorg.conf/XF86Config file as a skeleton, or use mine.
Edit each section to your specifications.  Be sure you use the correct
mouse setting, USB|PS/2|ttyS0.

-------------- next part --------------

# Xorg configuration created by system-config-display

Section "ServerLayout"
	Identifier     "Multihead layout"
	Screen      0  "Screen0" LeftOf "Screen1"
	Screen      1  "Screen1" 0 0
	InputDevice    "Mouse0" "CorePointer"
	InputDevice    "Keyboard0" "CoreKeyboard"
	Option	    "Xinerama" "off"
	Option	    "Clone" "on"
EndSection

Section "Files"

# RgbPath is the location of the RGB database.  Note, this is the name of the 
# file minus the extension (like ".txt" or ".db").  There is normally
# no need to change the default.
# Multiple FontPath entries are allowed (they are concatenated together)
# By default, Red Hat 6.0 and later now use a font server independent of
# the X server to render fonts.
	RgbPath      "/usr/X11R6/lib/X11/rgb"
	FontPath     "unix/:7100"
EndSection

Section "Module"
	Load  "dbe"
	Load  "extmod"
	Load  "fbdevhw"
	Load  "glx"
	Load  "record"
	Load  "freetype"
	Load  "type1"
	Load  "dri"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"

# Specify which keyboard LEDs can be user-controlled (eg, with xset(1))
#	Option	"Xleds"		"1 2 3"
# To disable the XKEYBOARD extension, uncomment XkbDisable.
#	Option	"XkbDisable"
# To customise the XKB settings to suit your keyboard, modify the
# lines below (which are the defaults).  For example, for a non-U.S.
# keyboard, you will probably want to use:
#	Option	"XkbModel"	"pc102"
# If you have a US Microsoft Natural keyboard, you can use:
#	Option	"XkbModel"	"microsoft"
#
# Then to change the language, change the Layout setting.
# For example, a german layout can be obtained with:
#	Option	"XkbLayout"	"de"
# or:
#	Option	"XkbLayout"	"de"
#	Option	"XkbVariant"	"nodeadkeys"
#
# If you'd like to switch the positions of your capslock and
# control keys, use:
#	Option	"XkbOptions"	"ctrl:swapcaps"
# Or if you just want both to be control, use:
#	Option	"XkbOptions"	"ctrl:nocaps"
#
	Identifier  "Keyboard0"
	Driver      "kbd"
	Option	    "XkbModel" "pc105"
	Option	    "XkbLayout" "us"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier  "Mouse0"
	Driver      "mouse"
	Option	    "Protocol" "IMPS/2"
	Option	    "Device" "/dev/input/mice"
	Option	    "ZAxisMapping" "4 5"
	Option	    "Emulate3Buttons" "yes"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier   "Monitor0"
	VendorName   "Monitor Vendor"
	ModelName    "Monitor 1280x1024"
	HorizSync    31.5 - 79.0
	VertRefresh  50.0 - 90.0
	Option	    "dpms"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier   "Monitor1"
	VendorName   "Monitor Vendor"
	ModelName    "Panasonic SL70i(TX-D7S36)"
	HorizSync    30.0 - 70.0
	VertRefresh  50.0 - 180.0
	Option	    "dpms"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier  "Videocard0"
	Driver      "radeon"
	VendorName  "Videocard vendor"
	BoardName   "ATI Radeon 9700 Pro"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier  "Videocard1"
	Driver      "radeon"
	VendorName  "Videocard Vendor"
	BoardName   "ATI Radeon 9700 Pro"
	BusID       "PCI:1:0:0"
	Screen      1
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier "Screen0"
	Device     "Videocard0"
	Monitor    "Monitor0"
	DefaultDepth     24
	SubSection "Display"
		Viewport   0 0
		Depth     24
		Modes    "1024x768" "800x600" "640x480"
	EndSubSection
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier "Screen1"
	Device     "Videocard1"
	Monitor    "Monitor1"
	DefaultDepth     24
	SubSection "Display"
		Viewport   0 0
		Depth     24
		Modes    "1024x768"
	EndSubSection
EndSection

Section "DRI"
	Group        0
	Mode         0666
EndSection

On Sat, 26 Mar 2005, Michael Harris wrote:

> Unable to find a valid frame buffer device.
> NV(0) Failed to open frame buffer device.
> Screens found but none have a usable configuration.

Mike,

   Look in the "Screens" section of XF86config-4. Make sure that the video
card matches the name in the "Driver" section and that the monitor name
matches the one in the "Monitor" section. Check case and punctuation very
carefully. This is what usually causes the last message above. Fix that and
all problems should go away.

> p.s.  is there a way for me to send mail from my shell?

   pine
   mutt
   elm
   mail

Rich

Why don't internet businesses use the abuse at domain.com convention? It's an
easy conventoin to remember if you want to help gether evidence of email
avuse, and using it makes reporting abuse quick and easy. THere's nothing
more irritating than to take the time to report abuse (making sure the
headers are included, etc.) only to find out that either that address is
no good or they want you to go to the their web site and fill out a form!
I guess what it says to me is that they really DON'T want you to bother
them with abuse reports.

From rshepard at appl-ecosys.com  Mon Mar 28 08:57:32 2005
From: rshepard at appl-ecosys.com (Rich Shepard)
Date: Mon, 28 Mar 2005 08:57:32 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] Avoiding unwanted e-mail on Comcast
In-Reply-To: <200503280826.56659.rsteff.l@comcast.net>
References: <200503271825.37380.rsteff.l@comcast.net>
	<200503272012.57612.baloo@ursine.ca>
	<200503280826.56659.rsteff.l@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0503280844560.10439@salmo.appl-ecosys.com>

On Mon, 28 Mar 2005, Richard C. Steffens wrote:

> Ok, a "duh!" moment. While I've been semi aware of abuse@, it never sunk in
> that just forwarding spam to the serving ISP was a thing I should do. But,
> isn't that just confirming a live address to the spammer running his own
> ISP? Do I need to move up a level to the ISP's ISP? Sounds like I've got
> more reading to do. Any recommended source for this kind of spam fighting
> information?

Dick,

   I don't know if spammers run their own provider services. I suspect not
because they'd be kicked off too often. However, the domain name in the
"From: " line is almost always either spoofed or made up. A dead giveaway is
when you see the "Received from: " line that has "madeupname.com (unknown
[xx.xxx.xx.xxx])" where the xx represents the originating IP address.

   Use that IP address with the "whois" command and you'll find the actual
name of the originating ISP. Usually these now come in a single hop, or the
hop before is also forged and it's an IANA-reserved IP address. So I report
it to the address from which I received it and let them trace it back if it's
not one of their customers.

   SpamCop and SpamHaus are good sources of information.

> In any event, reporting is not something many of my friends will want to
> do, or even understand. So, for them, is my idea of having them establish
> their primary account with Comcast as a throw-away name and their preferred
> addresses as secondary accounts a reasonable thing for them to do, or is
> there some gotcha I'm not thinking of?

   Reporting spam is analagous to reporting a robbery. If one does the
reporting there's a chance the robber will be caught or the spammer
disconnected. Most of the time the ISP tells the "spammer" that her machine
has been compromised and to get it cleaned up or lose the account. If you do
nothing then you let them mug us unmolested.

   When I see an IP address from one of the larger providers I take the time
to report it because 1) they almost always take action to prevent it
happening again from that customer and B) it provides jobs for all the
techies who chase these down and follow up on them. However, when the IP
address is part of a block assigned to countries that 1) don't seem to care
about spammers (or eagerly sell them bandwidth as long as the spammer keeps
paying) or B) from whom I would never expect legitimate e-mail, I reject the
IP address block at the MTA level. That's the major reason I brought the mail
server in-house rather than leaving it at my ISP.

   Indifference to spam costs all of us time and money. Both directly and
indirectly. Perhaps it's worth considering educating family and friends on
why spam should be reported and how to do so.

Rich

-- 
Dr. Richard B. Shepard, President
Applied Ecosystem Services, Inc. (TM)
<http://www.appl-ecosys.com>   Voice: 503-667-4517   Fax: 503-667-8863

Quoting "Richard C. Steffens" <rsteff.l at comcast.net>:

> On Monday 28 March 2005 7:06 am, Rich Shepard wrote:
> > On Sun, 27 Mar 2005, Paul Johnson wrote:
> > > Just hitting delete never solves the answer, reporting does work.
> >
> >    I just had an interesting experiece. I forwarded a spam message to the
> > originating ISP only to have them bounce it with their spam filters! Yes,
> I
> > used "abuse at ...". Strange. So I now reject their entire IP address block.
> 
> Ok, a "duh!" moment. While I've been semi aware of abuse@, it never sunk in 
> that just forwarding spam to the serving ISP was a thing I should do. But, 
> isn't that just confirming a live address to the spammer running his own ISP?
> 
> Do I need to move up a level to the ISP's ISP?

Yes.  If it appears that an  ISP  is not responsive to complaints or is in fact
part of the problem, you then pester their upstream peers.  If the problem is
that serious, I would bring in extra help (Like spamhaus), as some ISPs have
been known to turn a blind eye to spamming activity.  


I've heard tales that the most successful tactic to countering spam is to try to
get a phone number or real address of the spammer's clients or anyone
facilitating them.  This can be almost impossible sometimes, but occasionally
it's possible to find out who's actually making the  money selling the penis
pills..  These individuals and organizations usually have 800 or other types of
toll free numbers, and I've heard that disgruntled spam victims are sometimes
prone to war dialing these 800 numbers every minute until the Spammer signs a
pledge to never do so again.

Of course, I've only heard of such things happening... and I don't actually
recommend that you engage in any of the harassment tactics described above.

 
Regards,
Max

From 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com  Mon Mar 28 15:13:55 2005
From: 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com (Steve Bonds)
Date: Mon, 28 Mar 2005 15:13:55 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Ext2/3 Undelete
Message-ID: <30483-41562@sneakemail.com>

Linux Folks:

A combination of unfortunate factors has led to an important file
being deleted from a system that normally needs no backups.  (Isn't
that where ALL the important files are deleted?)  Normally I'd just
regenerate this system from our kickstart image, but the file in
question is a logfile holding debug data for a problem that only
recurs every few months.  If I can avoid waiting for the next
occurrence, I'd like to.

The process writing the log file is still running, so I can grab the
inode number from "lsof" and the OS has not re-used the blocks holding
the data.  I figure I have a few options:

1) "dd" the raw filesystem to another host and use "debugfs" to change
the inode number of some random file on the same filesystem to point
to the blocks holding the data I want, then mount the modified
filesystem and copy this "file" somewhere safe.

2) Use "e2image" to do basically the above since debugfs mentions that
it operates on e2image files, but doesn't mention if the above "dd"-ed
filesystem image will work

3) Use some free Linux file recovery tool.  Google offers few
options-- do any of these work on a "dd"-ed file system image?  (I'm
certainly not going to risk the original!)
  + "r-undelete" frequently mentioned, but not free, despite what their ads say.
  + "r-linux", same company, seems free but is a Windows executable.  How odd.
  + http://www1.lunetix.de/download/ ("undelete")

What would you all suggest?

  -- Steve Bonds

other tools.

From 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com  Mon Mar 28 17:12:02 2005
From: 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com (Steve Bonds)
Date: Mon, 28 Mar 2005 17:12:02 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Ext2/3 Undelete
In-Reply-To: <30483-41562@sneakemail.com>
References: <30483-41562@sneakemail.com>
Message-ID: <21118-04101@sneakemail.com>

On Mon, 28 Mar 2005 15:13:55 -0800, Steve Bonds wrote:

> 1) "dd" the raw filesystem to another host and use "debugfs" to change
> the inode number of some random file on the same filesystem to point
> to the blocks holding the data I want, then mount the modified
> filesystem and copy this "file" somewhere safe.

Thanks for the tip on The Sleuth Kit.  I have a copy of Helix, but
their documentation is incredibly poor.

I ended up recovering the file via debugfs, but I noticed some strange
behavior.  On the image file I created with "dd", the deleted inode
referenced a chain of filesystem block containing nothing but zeroes. 
However, on the running system the same inode referenced a chain of
filesystem blocks containing the actual log file data.  (I.e. the
contents of the file produced by the debugfs command "dump
<inode-number> /tmp/local_file" were different when run on the image
vs. the live system.)

I don't understand why a "dd" wouldn't capture the whole thing unless
it were stuck in the filesystem write cache.  This log file is months
old, so I can't imagine it being kept in cache that long.

Any ideas on why the captured image wouldn't reflect what was obtained
from the running system?

  -- Steve

On Mon, 28 Mar 2005 17:12:02 -0800, Steve Bonds wrote:

> I ended up recovering the file via debugfs, but I noticed some strange
> behavior.  On the image file I created with "dd", the deleted inode
> referenced a chain of filesystem block containing nothing but zeroes.
> However, on the running system the same inode referenced a chain of
> filesystem blocks containing the actual log file data.  (I.e. the
> contents of the file produced by the debugfs command "dump
> <inode-number> /tmp/local_file" were different when run on the image
> vs. the live system.)

I've chalked this up to something not quite right in debugfs' handling
of filesystem image files.  The Sleuth Kit's "icat" command recovered
the missing data perfectly from the same image file that debugfs
recovered only zeroes.

  -- Steve


From fpikus at gmail.com  Mon Mar 28 16:35:20 2005
From: fpikus at gmail.com (Fedor Pikus)
Date: Mon, 28 Mar 2005 16:35:20 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Ext2/3 Undelete
In-Reply-To: <30483-41562@sneakemail.com>
References: <30483-41562@sneakemail.com>
Message-ID: <a4fbdc7b05032816351e6a1601@mail.gmail.com>

Depends on whether it's ext2 or ext3. If it's ext2, you should be able
to recover, there are several tools which can help:

http://recover.sourceforge.net/linux/recover/
http://e2undel.sourceforge.net/

But if it's ext3, the outlook is much worse. Some tools claim to help,
like this one
http://www.sleuthkit.org
or commercial Phoenix Linux.

From john at johntelford.com  Mon Mar 28 21:38:34 2005
From: john at johntelford.com (John Telford)
Date: Mon, 28 Mar 2005 21:38:34 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Holy Troika
Message-ID: <r02010500-1038-CBAC497EA01411D9981E000A959F4BC6@[172.27.1.100]>

Recent PLUG threads have been discussing flaky Comcast, flaky DNS, and
flaky email services.  We might as well throw in flaky Web services just
for the heck of it.

My defense strategy against these flakes is the Holy Troika.  My
experience is by keeping the ISP separate from DNS services, and
both separate from email and Web services, helps me keep my options
open and my sanity too.  My particular troika is Comcast for ISP,
register.com for DNS services, and Interland for both email and Web
services.  The Holy Troika enables me to radically alter any or all
of the services while keeping a consistent Internet domain address. 
Clients appreciate this.

<rant>
Back in the bad old days before using the Holy Troika, I inevitably
experienced spotty service, and out right stupidity when dealing with
ISPs.  I'm sad to say, it was a rare ISP who could even spell DNS let
alone understand changing an MX record.  The most difficult part was
usually changing domain registrar.  Hopefully, things have improved in
the ISP world.
</rant>

I've lost track of how many times the local cable service, now Comcast,
has changed ownership.  Each regime change requires subscribers using
the cable companies DNS, email, and Web services to sooner or later make
domain name changes.  I've ridden out these ownership storms by simply
rebooting the cable modem.

The Holy Troika has a down side, cost.  Keeping a consistent Internet
domain address, while being able to quickly change any pieces of the
troika, is worth it to me and my businesses.

...John

From 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com  Tue Mar 29 11:52:44 2005
From: 1s7k8uhcd001 at sneakemail.com (Steve Bonds)
Date: Tue, 29 Mar 2005 11:52:44 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] edit lines in a text file
In-Reply-To: <4249AE41.2080502@aracnet.com>
References: <4249AE41.2080502@aracnet.com>
Message-ID: <1664-30806@sneakemail.com>

On Tue, 29 Mar 2005 11:36:33 -0800, Maodhog wrote:

> I want to take a text file, made up of email addresses and chop the
> users name off the domain name so I can uniq -u the domains.
> 
> I can't remember what the command is to remove all before the character
> "X"(which in this case is the @ sign).

awk -F@ '{print $2}' < your_file

or...

perl -p -e 's/^[^\@]+\@//' < your_file

or...

perl -n -e 'chomp; if (/\@(.*)$/) { print "$1\n" }' < your_file

And so on.  ;-)  Each responds slightly differently to malformed
input, so choose and adjust as is appropriate for the mangled files
you're likely to see.

  -- Steve

From heinlein at madboa.com  Tue Mar 29 12:06:54 2005
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Tue, 29 Mar 2005 12:06:54 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] edit lines in a text file
In-Reply-To: <1664-30806@sneakemail.com>
References: <4249AE41.2080502@aracnet.com> <1664-30806@sneakemail.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.OSX.4.62.0503291156390.1573@arrowhead.galois.com>

On Tue, 29 Mar 2005, Steve Bonds wrote:

> On Tue, 29 Mar 2005 11:36:33 -0800, Maodhog wrote:
>
>> I want to take a text file, made up of email addresses and chop the 
>> users name off the domain name so I can uniq -u the domains.
>>
>> I can't remember what the command is to remove all before the 
>> character "X"(which in this case is the @ sign).
>
> awk -F@ '{print $2}' < your_file
> perl -p -e 's/^[^\@]+\@//' < your_file
> perl -n -e 'chomp; if (/\@(.*)$/) { print "$1\n" }' < your_file

sed 's!^.*@!!' your_file

cut -d@ -f2 < your_file

I find that GNU sed is typically faster than any other solution, but 
the real time difference is probably insignificant in a job like 
yours.

Oh, to sort the domain names in a way that takes subdomains into 
account, try

sed 's!^.*@!!' your_file | sort -t. -k 3,3 -k 2,2 -k 1,1 | uniq

This recipe assumes no more than 3 levels of subdomains in any given 
address. I assume you can figure out how to adjust the recipe if you 
know that you have more or fewer...

--Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

From max.reid at saikonetworks.com  Tue Mar 29 14:51:28 2005
From: max.reid at saikonetworks.com (max.reid at saikonetworks.com)
Date: Tue, 29 Mar 2005 14:51:28 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Holy Troika
In-Reply-To: <r02010500-1038-CBAC497EA01411D9981E000A959F4BC6@[172.27.1.100]>
References: <r02010500-1038-CBAC497EA01411D9981E000A959F4BC6@[172.27.1.100]>
Message-ID: <1112136688.4249dbf0a038b@webmail.no-ip.com>

Quoting John Telford <john at johntelford.com>:

> 
> I've lost track of how many times the local cable service, now Comcast,
> has changed ownership.  Each regime change requires subscribers using
> the cable companies DNS, email, and Web services to sooner or later make
> domain name changes.  I've ridden out these ownership storms by simply
> rebooting the cable modem.
> 
> The Holy Troika has a down side, cost.  Keeping a consistent Internet
> domain address, while being able to quickly change any pieces of the
> troika, is worth it to me and my businesses.

Hmm...If redundancy and flexibility are your primary drivers,  your cost factor
issue could be mitigated somewhat by running your own servers.  Only "costs"
besides hardware at this point would  be to purchase commodity transit from a
variety of ISPs or colocation providers.  Once you pinpoint your capacity
requirements, handling things like redundancy is pretty trivial and not that
expensive with DNS and SMTP.

Handling Web services or web applications can get a little tricky, but a good
reverse proxy solution can typically handle load distribution with everything
but the most complex web applications.


Regards,
Max
