From plug_0 at robinson-west.com  Tue Mar 29 14:24:55 2005
From: plug_0 at robinson-west.com (plug_0 at robinson-west.com)
Date: Tue, 29 Mar 2005 14:24:55 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Postfix
Message-ID: <1112135095.4249d5b7ded70@xerxes.robinson-west.com>

smtpd_recipient_restrictions =
                                     reject_non_fqdn_sender,
                                  reject_non_fqdn_recipient,
                               reject_unknown_sender_domain,
                            reject_unknown_recipient_domain,
                                          permit_mynetworks,
                                  reject_unauth_destination,
               check_policy_service unix:private/policy-spf,
        check_sender_access hash:/etc/postfix/sender_access,
                                  reject_unlisted_recipient,
          check_policy_service unix:private/policy-greylist,
                           reject_rbl_client dnsbl.ahbl.org,
                          reject_rbl_client opm.blitzed.org,
                            reject_rbl_client list.dsbl.org,
                           reject_rbl_client hil.habeas.com,
                           reject_rbl_client bl.spamcop.net,
                         reject_rbl_client psbl.surriel.com,
                          reject_rbl_client cbl.abuseat.org,
                          reject_rbl_client dnsbl.sorbs.net,
               reject_rhsbl_sender bogusmx.rfc-ignorant.com,
                reject_rhsbl_sender bulk.rhs.mailpolice.com,
                reject_rhsbl_sender porn.rhs.mailpolice.com,
                   reject_rhsbl_sender dsn.rfc-ignorant.org,
            reject_rhsbl_sender postmaster.rfc-ignorant.org,
                 reject_rhsbl_sender abuse.rfc-ignorant.org,
                #reject_rhsbl_sender whois.rfc-ignorant.org,  # This no work.
                                                     permit

Okay, the line that says "This no work." catches some sites 
that it shouldn't.  I'd like to use the test.  I need a 
way to explicitly ignore it for certain smtp sources that 
won't pass, but are valid.

If I understand correctly, Postfix continues to process until
a test fails or the permit line.  What I want to do is 
short cut past these tests for certain trusted domains that 
are likely to fail multiple checks even though they are valid
email sources.  

I want:
     smtpd_recipient_restrictions = permit

for specific email sources.



Seperate problem, greylisting error...

This is postfix-2.1.1, is there an easy way to change the smtp
450 Service is unavailable message to a greylisting for n 
seconds message instead?  I want my smtp error responses 
to be as specific as possible.



Seperate problem, using helo checking...

Any number of sites, such as hotmail for one, don't set their helo 
to the hostname of the server they're using.  I've noticed trouble 
with ebay too.  Is helo checking a worthless thing to do?  Is the 
helo string ambiguous and worthless information?
Is there any standard that is adhered to widely for the helo?  
It seems that a helo being a host name that resolves to the
connected from ip is smart.  The intended recipient smtp 
server can do a comparison, if you can't fool the recipient 
smtp server when it tries to determine what the connected 
from ip is.  How prevalent is ip spoofing?  Can ip spoofing 
be defeated?



Seperate problem, sender verification...

I've heard of smtp authentication, but what's the point if someone
can figure out what you're pasting to your email to get it accepted
and just copy cat what you're doing?  Seems to me that having your
trusted smtp sources make an ssh connection to you is the only way
to secure email transport over the Internet.  Can you run smtp over 
ssh?



Sending email to the Internet with proper headers...

My mailhub sitting on my lan seemingly can't :-(  Can I use
DNAT and SNAT with iptables to trick one of my external
relays into thinking that an smtp session initiated from
another computer on my lan is actually originating from it's 
loopback device?  The mail command on my relay seems to work
for sending email to anywhere with acceptable headers.

     --  Michael C. Robinson

>     smtpd_recipient_restrictions = permit/etc/postfix/whitelist
>
>for specific email sources.
>
>
>  
>
At the beginning of your smtpd_recipient_restrictions list, add this:

check_sender_access hash:/etc/postfix/whitelist

Then /etc/postfix/whitelist would contain:

someguy at someplace.com OK
somegal at someotherplace.com OK
@myhappyfunplace.com OK

Then run "postmap /etc/postfix/whitelist".

I'm out of time now, but the rest of your questions should be answerable 
with Google or searching the Postfix archives.
~M

>>>>> "Matt" == Matt Alexander <lowbassman at gmail.com> writes:

Matt> At the beginning of your smtpd_recipient_restrictions list, add this:

"Beginning"?  Since they are checked in that order, it'd be safer to
place exceptions just before the list that you're trying to provide an
exception for, so you can make a specific whitelist workaround.  (Also
keep in mind the DUNNO key... I'm using that in a few of my files.)

This also means that you should put cheap checks first, and expensive
checks last.  It's quite a nice feature.

Tcl/Tk 2005 First Call for papers.
===================================

Tcl/Tk 2005 will be held in Portland, Oregon USA in late October or early
November. The program committee asks all people using and developing with
Tcl/Tk and extensions to submit papers and proposals for presentations at
this conference.

Past conferences have seen submissions covering a wide variety of topics
including and not limited to:

    * Scientific and engineering applications
    * Industrial controls
    * Distributed applications and Network Managment
    * Object oriented extensions to Tcl/Tk
    * New widgets for Tk
    * Simulation and application steering with Tcl/Tk
    * Tcl/Tk-Centric operating environments
    * Tcl/Tk on small and embedded devices
    * Medical applications and visualization


At this point we are requesting submissions of:

    * Abstracts of papers for oral presentation.
    * Proposals for short courses to be taught the day prior to the conference.
    * Proposals for other presentations/discussions.
    * Proposals to present tutorial sessions.

Please send abstracts and proposals to tcl2005 (at) nscl (dot)
msu (dot) edu

Important target dates:
=======================
  July  1, 2005    - Abstracts and proposals due.
  July 31, 2005    - Notification to authors.
  Sep  15, 2005    - Author materials due.

The submissions should consist of an abstract of about 100 words and a
summary of maximum two pages. Omit extraneous or redundant information.
Length is not a direct factor in judging the quality of the submission.

The authors of oral presentations will have 20-25 minutes to present the
paper at the conference.

The program committee will review and evaluate papers according to the
following criteria:

    * Quantity and quality of novel content
    * Relevance and interest to the Tcl/Tk community
    * Suitability of content for presentation at the conference

Proposals may report on commercial or non-commercial systems, but those with
only blatant marketing content will not be accepted.

Application and experience papers need to strike a balance between background
on the application domain and the relevance of Tcl/Tk to the application.
Application and experience papers should clearly explain how the application
or experience illustrates a novel use of Tcl/Tk, and what lessons the Tcl/Tk
community can derive from the application or experience to apply to their own
development efforts.

Papers accompanied by non-disclosure agreement forms will be returned to the
author(s) unread. All submissions are held in the highest confidentiality
prior to publication in the Proceedings, both as a matter of policy and in
accord with the U. S. Copyright Act of 1976.

The primary author for each accepted paper will receive registration to the
Technical Sessions portion of the conference at a reduced rate.

The program committee also welcomes proposals for panel discussions of up to
90 minutes. Proposals should include a list of confirmed panelists, a title
and format, and a panel description with position statements from each
panelist. Panels should have no more than four speakers, including the panel
moderator, and should allow time for substantial interaction with attendees.
Panels are not presentations of related research papers.

Program Committee:
==================
  Donal  Fellows       University of Manchester
  Clif   Flynt         Noumena Corp.
  Ron    Fox           NSCL Michigan State University
  Jeff   Hobbs         ActiveState Corp.
  Steve  Landers       Digital Smarties
  Gerald Lester        HMS Software
  Cyndy  Lilagan       Eolas Technologies Inc.
  Arjen  Markus        WL | Delft Hydraulics

--
Sincerely,
 	Andreas Kupries <akupries at shaw.ca>
 			<http://www.purl.org/NET/akupries/>

Subject: [PLUG] Open Office Spreadsheet - Center across columns
Message-ID: <200503301003.20958.rsteff.l@comcast.net>

In Excel, one may select several contiguous cells in a row and designate that 
the content of the first cell be centered across all of those cells. A useful 
purpose for this is when one has two rows of header information and groups 
parts of the second row with a title in one cell of the first row.

Example:

------------------------------------
|                       Miles                     |
------------------------------------
|     In        |      Out     |     Total    |
------------------------------------
|                |                |                 |

Is there a way to do this in Open Office's spreadsheet?

On Wed, 30 Mar 2005, Bill Spears wrote:

> Not to encourage infidelity, but has anyone else moved an account 
> from Fedora to Mac OS X?  I guess the main point would be moving 
> from Evolution to ?. I believe Firefox is available for Mac.

I use Linux at home and Mac OS X at work. The only way I know to 
maintain compatibility between mail clients on both platforms is to 
use standards-based network protocols: IMAP for mail, LDAP for 
addresses. Otherwise, data will get lost, no doubt about it...

That said, you might be able to get Evolution to compile and run on a 
Mac -- but that's only a guess. I can say, however, that the Mozilla 
Thunderbird mail client works quite well on OS X. (Pine, too, but 
that's a fairly acquired taste these days. :-)

Also, many people know and like the Apple Mail client.

--Paul Heinlein <heinlein at madboa.com>

One interesting alternative to both managed servers and your own
colo box is a virtual colo set up with User Mode Linux.  I have such
a "machine" at vcolo.com, costing me $23/month.  I serve 8 websites
(one added today, took 5 minutes), 4 mailing lists, 3 wikis, and a
subversion development server off it, and back it up to my office
backup server (dirvish, of course), over a VPN tunnel.

These are normally $20/mo, but I added an extra IP address to do
Randal's high-MX spam trapping, and added 2GB of disk space for
an onsite backup of the machine.  I hope to have 15 second
scriptkiddy detection and alternate image reboot someday.

I hope to have a presentation ready for PLUG or Advanced Topics
Real Soon Now.  One more test will be to see if I can do a live
failover to a different ISP, probably Rimuhosting of New Zealand by
way of Dallas.  This would give me 10Gbps connectivity, meaning I
could use up my monthly bandwidth allotment in under 30 seconds ...

From wcooley at nakedape.cc  Wed Mar 30 17:14:31 2005
From: wcooley at nakedape.cc (Wil Cooley)
Date: Wed, 30 Mar 2005 17:14:31 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Fun crypto project
Message-ID: <1112231671.4446.46.camel@denk>


So I'm fighting with merging saved passwords between Mozilla and
Firefox.  I've decided that the easiest thing to do is to understand how
to decrypt the password strings.  I've "removed" my master password for
the time being, which AFAICT just means they're encrypted with an empty
string for key.  I can parse the actual content of the password file,
but what I do not understand ASN.1 encoding and all that stuff well
enough to get past 'bad magic number' from 'openssl'.  (Oh yeah, I
figured trying to use the openssl command-line tools would be the
quickest path to understanding this stuff.)

To start with, here's an encrypted string, stored in a file called 'p':

MDIEEPgAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAEwFAYIKoZIhvcNAwcECBN1DvAmjAkIBAhVWnt9v9k9Mw==

(The decrypted string is terribly interesting; it should be "wcooley".)

Here's the actual Seamonkey code:

http://lxr.mozilla.org/seamonkey/source/security/nss/lib/pk11wrap/pk11sdr.c#183

According to the comments, the data is DER-encoded, but it appears the
actual stored string is PEM-encoded (from what I understand, one is a
binary and the other ASCII representation of ASN.1-encoded data
structures).  I can use the OpenSSL 'asn1parse' command to actually view
the ASN.1 structure:

$ openssl asn1parse -inform PEM -in p -i 
    0:d=0  hl=2 l=  50 cons: SEQUENCE          
    2:d=1  hl=2 l=  16 prim:  OCTET STRING      
   20:d=1  hl=2 l=  20 cons:  SEQUENCE          
   22:d=2  hl=2 l=   8 prim:   OBJECT            :des-ede3-cbc
   32:d=2  hl=2 l=   8 prim:   OCTET STRING      
   42:d=1  hl=2 l=   8 prim:  OCTET STRING      

Ah, des-ede3-cbc!  That cipher corresponds with #defines in the code
(SEC_OID_DES_EDE3_CBC).  Well, this seems to be the obvious thing to
try, after reading over the 'enc(1)' man page:

openssl enc -des-ede3-cbc  -d -in p -salt
enter des-ede3-cbc decryption password:
(Nothing)

openssl enc -des-ede3-cbc  -d -in p -salt -k
bad magic number

Okay, maybe the 'enc' command doesn't want PEM; try to convert to DER
using 'asn1parse':

$ openssl asn1parse -inform PEM -in p -out p.der
...

Verify that it's DER:
$ file p.der
p.der: data
[wcooley at denk:~/tmp] *17:00:58*
$ openssl asn1parse -inform DER -in p.der -i
    0:d=0  hl=2 l=  50 cons: SEQUENCE          
    2:d=1  hl=2 l=  16 prim:  OCTET STRING      
   20:d=1  hl=2 l=  20 cons:  SEQUENCE          
   22:d=2  hl=2 l=   8 prim:   OBJECT            :des-ede3-cbc
   32:d=2  hl=2 l=   8 prim:   OCTET STRING      
   42:d=1  hl=2 l=   8 prim:  OCTET STRING      

After that, I've tried many permutations of things to use for key; the
only thing that gets anything other than 'bad magic number' is using '-K
0 -iv 0', which results in some fun binary data dumped to the screen and
a 'bad decrypt' error:

$ openssl enc -des-ede3-cbc  -d -in p.der -salt -p -K 0 -iv 0
salt=08DB2008912DF0B7
key=000000000000000000000000000000000000000000000000
iv =0000000000000000
5?
bad decrypt
9737:error:0606506D:digital envelope routines:EVP_DecryptFinal:wrong
final block length:evp_enc.c:431:

My guess at this point is that the 'enc' subcommand is expecting
unstructured data, but I'm giving it ASN.1 DER structures.  I cannot
find a way to extract the unstructured data or if I have, I haven't got
the right keys or something.  I've tried the '-strparse' option to
extract bytes 20-41 (extracting 22-31 results in an empty output file;
32-41 gives an error), but still no luck.

Anyone more crypto-savvy got any hints?

Wil
-- 
Wil Cooley                                 wcooley at nakedape.cc
Naked Ape Consulting                        http://nakedape.cc

On Wed, Mar 30, 2005 at 07:16:48PM +0000, rdought at pacifier.com wrote:
> bash-2.05b# mount /dev/hdc /mnt/cdrom
> mount: special device /dev/hdc does not exist
>

Not so obvious: If you've enabled IDE-SCSI for those drives, they'll
do that.  It's enabled at the kernel commandline, so you can do 
'cat /proc/cmdline' to see what it's being told.

In-Reply-To: <20050331041832.GH2010@bavariati.org>

On Wed, 30 Mar 2005 20:18:32 -0800
Aaron Burt <aaron at bavariati.org> wrote:

> Not so obvious: If you've enabled IDE-SCSI for those drives, they'll
> do that.  It's enabled at the kernel commandline, so you can do 
> 'cat /proc/cmdline' to see what it's being told.


That was the key.  This was in my /proc/cmdline:
	
	hdc=ide-scsi hdd=ide-scs

I commented those out and I had access to my drives again.

-----Original Message-----
From: plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org
[mailto:plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org] On Behalf Of Elliott Mitchell
Sent: Sunday, March 20, 2005 1:50 PM
To: plug at lists.pdxlinux.org
Subject: Re: [PLUG] FSCK what's going on?

>From: Carlos Konstanski <ckonstan at lunarlogic.com>  What do you mean 
>when you say "ran a fsck from knoppix"?  Did you run an  "e2fsck" 
>without the -f option, or did you run an actual "fsck"?  You  say the 
>checked out clean.  Was this right away when running the fsck  command, 
>or after a lengthy disk check?  e2fsck without a -f will often  not 
>even bother to run a disk check.

(Because it checks the clean flag on the filesystem, and unless there is a
panic or other unclean shutdown that does tend to get reset.)

> e2fsck is a wrapper around fsck.ext3.  I'm thinking it's kinda 
> pointless to run e2fsck.  Maybe use fsck directly instead.

Other way around. `fsck` is a pretty simple wrapper for `fsck.<fs>` (where
<fs> is "ext2", "ext3" or whatever). `fsck.ext2` and `fsck.ext3` are
generally symbolic links to `e2fsck`. The fun part is unless the FS is
actively marked as dirty (kernel checks found inconsistancies) or it has
exceeded the mount count, `fsck.ext3` is a no-op as it lets the kernel do
journal playback.

From griffint at pobox.com  Thu Mar 31 14:55:27 2005
From: griffint at pobox.com (Terry Griffin)
Date: Thu, 31 Mar 2005 14:55:27 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Adaptive firewall considerations
Message-ID: <20050331225527.GA21515@aracnet.com>

Hi all,

I'm toying around with some adaptive firewall ideas. In looking at the 
iptables logs and deciding what patterns might be worth adapting to, I've 
noticed that most of the hits coming from the outside are on TCP ports
135 and 445 (Windows RPC and DS respectively). Sometimes these hits come 
in big bunches, obvious attempts by a Win32-based worm to spread itself. 
But most of the time it's just a slow trickle.

So here's my question, and I guess it's more of a Windows question than
a Linux question, but trust me that the firewall runs Linux.

To what degree would a normally configured or typically misconfigured but 
*uninfected* Windows box try to connect to other random hosts on ports 
135 or 445? Is there some level of normal Window chat, or does *any* 
attempt to connect to our IP addresses from the outside on these ports 
indicate malicious intent?

If there is some normal level of chatter then I assume it would be limited 
to the immediate network on which the Windows box resides such that it 
might be normal to see this trickle of hits from the neighbors on our 
ISP's network, but hits to these ports from hosts in China would clearly 
be malicious. Yes? No?

Thanks,
Terry

From ehem at m5p.com  Thu Mar 31 14:51:51 2005
From: ehem at m5p.com (Elliott Mitchell)
Date: Thu, 31 Mar 2005 14:51:51 -0800 (PST)
Subject: [PLUG] FSCK what's going on?
In-Reply-To: <20050331200006.4454B427B@ulke.nakedape.cc>
Message-ID: <200503312251.j2VMppSv094066@m5p.com>

>From: "William A Morita" <wamorita at hevanet.com>
> Is there an easy way (and safe way) to set the dirty flag? 

Seems like something that should be added to `tune2fs`, but like Russ I
know of no handy way of doing so. Though `fsck -f` which forces, despite
the clean flag may be what you want. With most init script varients
creating the file "/forcefsck" will tell them to pass -f to fsck on
startup. Doing `touch /forcefsck` might be what you desire.

Tcl shells and precompilers have just recently been added to Cisco IOS in the
latest release train.  It is also used extensively in other newish network
management platforms (F5 networks, Inkra, ) to replace proprietary scripting
languages.  So I would necessarily say that it's dying if such features are
recently being incorporated in the these platforms.  Perhaps it's dying in the
context of gui stuff, but for tool command :-) related activities it seems to be
a sort of weird retro defacto standard.

Regards,
Max

Subject: [PLUG] Adaptive firewall considerations
In-Reply-To: <20050331225527.GA21515@aracnet.com>

On Mar 31, 2005 2:55 PM, Terry Griffin <griffint at pobox.com> wrote:
> Hi all,
> 
> I'm toying around with some adaptive firewall ideas. In looking at the
> iptables logs and deciding what patterns might be worth adapting to, I've
> noticed that most of the hits coming from the outside are on TCP ports
> 135 and 445 (Windows RPC and DS respectively). Sometimes these hits come
> in big bunches, obvious attempts by a Win32-based worm to spread itself.
> But most of the time it's just a slow trickle.
> 
> So here's my question, and I guess it's more of a Windows question than
> a Linux question, but trust me that the firewall runs Linux.
> 
> To what degree would a normally configured or typically misconfigured but
> *uninfected* Windows box try to connect to other random hosts on ports
> 135 or 445? Is there some level of normal Window chat, or does *any*
> attempt to connect to our IP addresses from the outside on these ports
> indicate malicious intent?
Port 135 is for directory replication
Port 445 is for SMB protocol over IP

So if you are wanting to replicate directories and share files over the internet
via IP then these need to be open.

> 
> If there is some normal level of chatter then I assume it would be limited
> to the immediate network on which the Windows box resides such that it
> might be normal to see this trickle of hits from the neighbors on our
> ISP's network, but hits to these ports from hosts in China would clearly
> be malicious. Yes? No?

Windows boxes do try to find each other and this is a polling operation
that occurs even when no connections are made.

First hit from google as to explain best methods of protection and
what the ports
do.
http://www.petri.co.il/what's_port_445_in_w2k_xp_2003.htm

On Thu, Mar 31, 2005 at 10:28:11AM -0800, William A Morita wrote:
> Elliott
> 
> Is there an easy way (and safe way) to set the dirty flag? 

You can force an fsck on the next boot by putting a file in /.
For Redhat, I think the file is /.autofsck and for Debian, it's /forcefsck

I have a box that I've been using as a file server/media server
everything else, including a PVR.

I recently added a Hauppauge PVR-350 card to the system and upgraded a
lot of software.  It all works but it's become very unstable.  It's
uptime is anywhere from 3 hours to 3 days, and not much more than that.
I've given up backing it up as I can't keep it up long enough to make a
backup.

It has 3 hard drive's on two separate controllers.  2 drive are in raid
1 and the other one was installed in the last 2 weeks and contains the
OS.

It's running debian unstable w/ a custom kernel.

The main error that I see is something like 

kernel: Trying to fix it up, but a reboot is needed



Tonight when I started looking again, I'm also seeing

hde2: rw=0, want=8761311624, limit=9767457
attempt to access beyond end of device

All that google produces on this is that it's a bug of the 2.2 kernel

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Thu Mar 31 21:31:37 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Thu, 31 Mar 2005 21:31:37 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Open Source TV-B-Gone?
Message-ID: <20050401053137.GA3676@gate.kl-ic.com>


By now, most of you have heard of the nifty new product TV-B-Gone,
a little $20 keyfob unit with an infrared emitter that mimics the
turn-off codes of thousands of different television sets.  It just
ships out ALL the turn-off codes in sequence, taking about 10 seconds
(and sometimes up to 70 seconds) to find the right code to turn off
a particular model of goddamnoisybox.  Just the thing when you are
in an airport waiting area and want to take a nap, or work on your
laptop, rather than listen to CNN blather. 

This was particularly acute in the Dallas airport a couple of weeks
ago;  blaring TVs all over the place, but all the wall sockets were
powered down so I could not charge my laptop.  

There is an open source "LIRC" project - Linux Infrared Remote Control -
that is working on using IrDA ports on laptops to remote-control TVs
and VCRs and the like.  Most Palm Pilots have IR ports for "beaming"
information to each other.  Perhaps you can guess where this is 
heading...

If there is some ambitious person on this list who is as annoyed
with gratuitous TV bombardment as I am, please consider designing an
open source program for Linux laptops that does the same thing as TV
B-Gone.  It could go one step further - there are only so many kinds
of television sets in a given airport, so after some experimentation
and community feedback, your could emit just the subset of codes that
worked in a particular place.  So you could type "tvoff phoenix" or
"tvoff logan" and get nearly instant response.

And for those of you who need their TV fix everywhere, all the time,
we will give you your own special place out on the sidewalk next to
the smokers you approved of evicting.

Keith
